<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction-to-reproductive-health-28-hours">INTRODUCTION TO REPRODUCTIVE HEALTH 28 HOURS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction-to-reproductive-health-28-hours" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="65f004aa">YEAR ONE, SEMESTER ONE – MARCH 2018 KECHN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#65f004aa" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="lecturer-rugendo-m-m-mr">LECTURER: RUGENDO.M.M.(MR.)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lecturer-rugendo-m-m-mr" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="module-competence">Module competence<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#module-competence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This module is designed to enable the learner to understand the background of RH and midwifery and apply knowledge of components, policies of RH and midwifery in provision of comprehensive and quality RH services</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="module-units">Module units<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#module-units" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Unit1: Fundamentals of Reproductive health 04 Hours</p>
<p>Unit 2: Anatomy and physiology of Reproductive system. 10 Hours</p>
<p>Unit 3: Sexuality; Sexual Health, Adolescent/Youth Health. 10 Hours</p>
<p>Unit 4: Safe Motherhood. 04 Hours</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="module-learning-outcomes">Module Learning Outcomes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#module-learning-outcomes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>At the end of this module, the learner should be able to: -</p>
<ol>
<li>Define terminologies in reproductive health</li>
<li>State RH policies, standards and guidelines</li>
<li>Outline the background and milestones of reproductive health and midwifery</li>
<li>Outline elements of quality of care in reproductive health services</li>
<li>Describe the anatomy and physiology of reproductive system</li>
<li>Discuss sexuality, sexual health and adolescent/youth health.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="module-content">Module Content<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#module-content" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Background of RH: Terminologies in reproductive health, policies, standards, guidelines; History and background of reproductive health. Elements of quality of care in reproductive health services. Concepts and history of reproductive health in Kenya. Components of reproductive health. History of midwifery: History of midwifery in ancient times; in developed world and in Kenya; Dynamics in midwifery.</li>
<li>Male reproductive system: Scrotum; testes; spermatogenesis; epididymis; vas deferens; spermatic cord; seminal vesicles; ejaculating duct; prostate glands; bulb urethral gland; penis.</li>
<li>Female Reproductive system: Female pelvis, bones, joints, ligaments, diameters, muscles, types of pelvis, pelvic deformities, female reproductive organs(external organs, internal organs, vagina, fallopian tubes, uterus ovaries)lymphatic supply, anatomical relations of reproductive organs to urethra, bladder, anus, rectum; structure and functions of female breast; physiology of lactation reproductive cycles;</li>
</ol>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>types of nipples; fertilization; implantation; embryology; foetal growth and development; foetal skull; foetal circulation; placenta at term</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Sexuality; Sexual Health, Adolescent/Youth Health: Sexual orientation; identity; body mapping; integration of sexual health into holistic care, attitude change towards sexuality and HIV-AIDS; youth sexual reproductive health needs; youth friendly services; roles of health care providers in promoting adolescent sexual and reproductive health.</li>
<li>Safe motherhood: Definition; Principles of safe motherhood, Objectives of safe motherhood; pillars of safe motherhood; strategies of achieving safe motherhood; challenges facing safe mother hood.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="teaching-and-learning-methods">TEACHING AND LEARNING METHODS:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#teaching-and-learning-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This course will be taught through various teaching and learning methods including and not limited to: lecture, demonstration, small group discussion, brainstorming, class presentation, and self-directed study, among others</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction-to-reproductive-health-and-midwifery">Introduction to Reproductive health and Midwifery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction-to-reproductive-health-and-midwifery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="learning-objectives">Learning objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#learning-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>By the end of the lesson the learner should be able to:</li>

</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction-to-midwifery">Introduction to midwifery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction-to-midwifery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Midwifery is a health care profession in which providers offer care to childbearing women during pregnancy, labour and birth, and during the postpartum period.</li>
<li>Midwives also help care for the new-born and assist the mother with breastfeeding.</li>
<li>A practitioner of midwifery is known as a midwife, a term used in reference to both women and men who have formal training in midwifery.</li>
<li>Midwives also provides care to women during pregnancy and birth and other services related to reproductive health such as family planning, postnatal services and post-abortion care and post rape care.</li>
<li>Midwives normally specializes in low-risk pregnancy, childbirth, and postpartum.</li>
<li>They are also trained to recognize and deal with deviations from the normal as well as certain high risk situations. Obstetricians, in contrast, are specialists in illness related to childbearing and in surgery.</li>
<li>Midwives are trained to handle certain more difficult deliveries, including breech births, twin births and births where the baby is in a posterior position, using non-invasive techniques.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="definition">Definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A midwife is a person who, having been regularly admitted to a midwifery educational program that is duly recognized in the country in which it is located, has successfully completed the prescribed course of studies in</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>midwifery and has acquired the requisite qualifications to be registered and/or legally licensed to practice midwifery.</p>
<ul>
<li>The midwife is recognized as a responsible and accountable professional who works in partnership with women to give the necessary support, care and advice during pregnancy, labour and the postpartum period.</li>
<li>This care includes preventive measures, the promotion of normal birth, the detection of complications in mother and child, accessing of medical or other appropriate assistance and the carrying out of emergency measures.</li>
<li>The midwife has an important task in health counselling and education, not only for the woman, but also within the family and community.</li>
<li>This work should involve antenatal education and preparation for parenthood and may extend to women's health, sexual or reproductive health and childcare.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="roles-of-a-midwife">ROLES OF A MIDWIFE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#roles-of-a-midwife" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Typical duties of a midwife include:</li>
<li>☑ Examining and monitoring pregnant women</li>
<li>☑ Assessing care requirements/writing care plans</li>
<li>☑ Undertaking antenatal care in hospitals, homes and GP practices</li>
<li>☑ Carrying out screening tests</li>
<li>☑ Providing information, emotional support and reassurance to women and their partners</li>
<li>☑ Taking patient samples, pulses, temperatures and blood pressures</li>
<li>☑ Caring for and assisting women in labour</li>
<li>☑ Monitoring and administering medication, injections and intravenous infusions during labour</li>
<li>☑ Monitoring the foetus during labour</li>
<li>☑ Advising about and supporting parents in the daily care of their newborn babies</li>
<li>☑ Helping parents to cope with miscarriage, termination, stillbirth and neonatal death</li>
<li>☑ Writing records</li>
<li>☑ Tutoring student midwives.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="key-skills-for-midwives">Key skills for midwives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#key-skills-for-midwives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>☑ Good health and fitness</li>
<li>☑ Excellent teamwork skills</li>
<li>☑ Interpersonal skills</li>
<li>☑ Communication skills</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-code-of-conduct-and-regulation-for-midwives">The Code of conduct and regulation for midwives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-code-of-conduct-and-regulation-for-midwives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="i-midwifery-relationships">I. Midwifery Relationships<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#i-midwifery-relationships" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A. Midwives respect a woman's informed right of choice and promote the woman's acceptance of responsibility for the outcomes of her choices.</p>
<p>B. Midwives work with women, supporting their right to participate actively in decisions about their care, and empowering women to speak for themselves on issues affecting the health of women and their families in their culture/society.</p>
<p>C. Midwives, together with women, work with policy and funding agencies to define women's needs for health services and to ensure that resources are fairly allocated considering priorities and availability.</p>
<p>D. Midwives support and sustain each other in their professional roles, and actively nurture their own and others' sense of self-worth.</p>
<p>E. Midwives work with other health professionals, consulting and referring as necessary when the woman's need for care exceeds the competencies of the midwife.</p>
<p>F. Midwives recognize the human interdependence within their field of practice and actively seek to resolve inherent conflicts.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ii-practice-of-midwifery">II. Practice of Midwifery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ii-practice-of-midwifery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A. Midwives provide care for women and childbearing families with respect for cultural diversity while also working to eliminate harmful practices within those same cultures.</p>
<p>B. Midwives encourage realistic expectations of childbirth by women within their own society, with the minimum expectation that no women should be harmed by conception or childbearing.</p>
<p>C. Midwives use their professional knowledge to ensure safe birthing practices in all environments and cultures.</p>
<p>D. Midwives respond to the psychological, physical, emotional and spiritual needs of women seeking health care, whatever their circumstances.</p>
<p>E. Midwives act as effective role models in health promotion for women throughout their life cycle, for families and for other health professionals.</p>
<p>F. Midwives actively seek personal, intellectual and professional growth throughout their midwifery career, integrating this growth into their practice.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="iii-the-professional-responsibilities-of-midwives">III. The Professional Responsibilities of Midwives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iii-the-professional-responsibilities-of-midwives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A. Midwives hold in confidence client information in order to protect the right to privacy, and use judgment in sharing this information.</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>B. Midwives are responsible for their decisions and actions, and are accountable for the related outcomes in their care of women.
C. Midwives may refuse to participate in activities for which they hold deep moral opposition; however, the emphasis on individual conscience should not deprive women of essential health services.
D. Midwives participate in the development and implementation of health policies that promote the health of all women and childbearing families.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="iv-advancement-of-midwifery-knowledge-and-practice">IV. Advancement of Midwifery Knowledge and Practice<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iv-advancement-of-midwifery-knowledge-and-practice" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A. Midwives ensure that the advancement of midwifery knowledge is based on activities that protect the rights of women as persons.
B. Midwives develop and share midwifery knowledge through a variety of processes, such as peer review and research.
C. Midwives participate in the formal education of midwifery students and midwives.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="v-ethical-principles-in-midwifery-practice">V. Ethical principles in midwifery practice.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#v-ethical-principles-in-midwifery-practice" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A. Midwife should uphold ethical principles and expectations in executing his/her duties.
B. Some of the ethical principles in midwifery practice include: -
i. Autonomy
ii. Beneficence
iii. Veracity
iv. Non-maleficence
v. Fidelity
vi. Justice
vii. Self-care.
&gt; NB: Read on each of the above ethical principles.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reproductive-health">Reproductive Health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reproductive-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li><strong>Definition</strong>: Reproductive Health is a state of complete physical, mental, emotional and social well-being and not merely absence of disease or infirmity in all matters relating to the reproductive health system and its functions and processes. (ICPD 1994).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="components-of-reproductive-health">Components of reproductive Health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#components-of-reproductive-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Safe motherhood, Maternal and Neonatal Health</li>
<li>Family Planning</li>
<li>Adolescent / Youth Sexual reproductive health,</li>
<li>Gender issues, sexual and reproductive health rights</li>
</ol>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Reproductive Tract Infections (RTIs)</li>
<li>Infertility</li>
<li>Cancer of Reproductive Organs</li>
<li>Reproductive Health for Elderly Persons</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="elements-of-quality-reproductive-health">Elements of quality reproductive health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#elements-of-quality-reproductive-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Elements of quality reproductive health care include: -</li>
<li>a) Technical competence</li>
<li>b) Good interpersonal relationship</li>
<li>c) Mechanisms to encourage continuity</li>
<li>d) Integration of services</li>
<li>e) Provision of factual information and counselling</li>
<li>f) Availability of services</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reproductive-health-policy">Reproductive health policy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reproductive-health-policy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A policy is an official statement that is issued by the government or any other agency to guide its workers on what to do.</li>
<li>It defines the decided course of action by the government or any organization.</li>
<li>Policy guidelines refers to written instructions that give directives in relation to the practices that are supposed to be followed or adhered to while providing services to the clients and public in general.</li>
<li>Reproductive health policy therefore refers to the official statement and guidelines issued by the government to guide provision of reproductive health services.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aims-and-objectives-of-reproductive-health-policies-and-guidelines">Aims and objectives of reproductive health policies and guidelines<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aims-and-objectives-of-reproductive-health-policies-and-guidelines" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Reduce maternal, perinatal and neonatal morbidity and mortality;</li>
<li>Reduce unmet family planning needs</li>
<li>Improve sexual and reproductive health of adolescents and youth;</li>
<li>Promote gender equity and equality in matters of reproductive health, including access to appropriate services;</li>
<li>Contribute to reduction of the HIV/AIDS burden and improvement of the RH status of infected and affected persons;</li>
<li>Reduce the burden of reproductive tract infections (RTIs) and improve access to, and quality of, RTI services;</li>
<li>Reduce the magnitude of infertility and increase access to efficient and effective investigative services for enhanced management of infertile individuals and couples;</li>
<li>Reduce morbidity and mortality associated with the common cancers of the reproductive organs in men and women.</li>
<li>Address RH-related needs of the elderly</li>
</ol>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<ol start="10">
<li>Address the special RH-related needs of people with disabilities.</li>
<li>Create awareness among leaders, communities and programme implementers of the need to promote high quality reproductive health services, in order to improve the well being of the people</li>
<li>Eliminate all forms of discrimination against women and female children to enable them to exercise their sexual and RH rights and to promote their equal representation in all levels of political and public life</li>
<li>Enhance both men and women's health throughout their life cycle</li>
<li>Provide quality and sustainable comprehensive RH services in all service delivery points (SDP's) and community levels.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="integration-of-reproductive-health-services">Integration of reproductive health services<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#integration-of-reproductive-health-services" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Integration is the process of by which various health services are provided at one delivery point.</li>
<li>It also includes the process by which the scope of provision of a particular service is expanded or broadened.</li>
<li>Integration of health services is referred to as supermarket approach of service delivery.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages-of-integration-of-reproductive-health-services">Advantages of integration of reproductive health services<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-integration-of-reproductive-health-services" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>It saves time</li>
<li>It promotes provision of more comprehensive services</li>
<li>It allows optimal utilization of available health care workers.</li>
<li>Allows for implementation of new patterns of health services</li>
<li>Helps in developing new technologies.</li>
<li>Helps in assessment of new needs and how they can be addressed in new ways.</li>
<li>Promote low cost of health care services.</li>
<li>It improves clients satisfaction</li>
<li>It ensures provision of efficient and cost effective reproductive health services</li>
<li>Ensures no missed opportunity in provision of patient's reproductive health needs</li>
<li>It promotes demand creation in provision of reproductive health services</li>
<li>Efficiency within the existing system so that key technical interventions can be provided up to the peripheral level</li>
<li>It improves reproductive health seeking behavior.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principles-for-effective-integration-of-reproductive-health-services">Principles for effective integration of Reproductive health services<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-for-effective-integration-of-reproductive-health-services" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>There should be intensive programme management.</li>
<li>There should be involvement of all departments in the facility.</li>
<li>There should be a coordinating committee in place</li>
<li>Plans and budgets should be shared with all stake holders.</li>
<li>Health standards, administrative policies and procedures should be well laid down and understood by all stakeholders.</li>
<li>There should be well and coordinated flow of information. Communication systems should be well understood.</li>
<li>There should be programmes involving different medical professionals</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<ul>
<li>There should be well laid quality monitoring and assurance procedures.</li>
<li>Patient information and referral programme should be well coordinated.</li>
<li>There should be a well established human resource development and management</li>
<li>There should be effective Integration of reproductive health services including training</li>
<li>Appropriate Identification, mobilization and allocation of resources.</li>
<li>Operational research in reproductive health and monitoring and evaluation as well as supervision</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sexuality">Sexuality<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sexuality" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Sexuality refers to one's self sexual being which includes sexual feeling, attraction, behaving, dressing and communicating in sexual manner.</li>
<li>Sexuality includes feeling, thinking or behaving as a male of female.</li>
<li>Sexuality also extends to being sexually attractive, being in love and being in relationship with sexual intimacy and sexual activities.</li>
<li>Sexuality includes Intimacy—the need and ability to be emotionally close to another human being and have that closeness reciprocated.</li>
<li>Sexual identity—This is a person's understanding of who he or she is sexually.</li>
<li>Sexual identity involves:-</li>
<li>Gender identity (I'm I male or female)</li>
<li>Gender role (what a man or woman can or cannot do because of their gender)</li>
<li>Sexual orientation (who am I attracted to sexually? (Heterosexual, homosexual)</li>
<li>Sexual preferences (what are my sexual limits? Monogamy? Polygamy? Bigamy?)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="psychophysiology-of-sex-response">Psychophysiology of sex response.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychophysiology-of-sex-response" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Normal sexual behaviour has four phases in sexual response cycle:</p>
<p>I. Excitement
II. Plateau
III. Orgasm
IV. Resolution</p>
<p>I. Excitement/ Arousal: it is psychological stimulation or fantasy in presence of a love object</p>
<p>It consists of: -
a) Sexual drive
b) Sexual motivation
c) Sexual wish</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>II. Plateau: It is physiological sexual stimulation of the body. This stage is characterized by: -</p>
<ul>
<li>In male's penile tumescence and erection occurs</li>
<li>Vaginal lubrication</li>
<li>Venous engorgement of external genitalia</li>
<li>Vaginal barrel constricts</li>
<li>Clitoris enlarge and retract</li>
<li>Specific colour changes of genitalia.</li>
<li>Breast size enlarges by 25%</li>
<li>Testicular elevation occurs</li>
<li>Voluntary contraction of large muscles</li>
<li>Lasts for about 30seconds.</li>
<li>May last for few minutes to hours</li>
</ul>
<p>III. Orgasm: This is the peak of sexual pleasure. This stage is characterized by:</p>
<ul>
<li>Contraction of the outer third of the vagina</li>
<li>Swelling of the outer third of the vagina which reduces its diameter by half. This reduction in diameter increases the friction stimulation of the penis.</li>
<li>Rhythmic contraction of perineal muscles</li>
<li>In male ejaculation takes place</li>
<li>Vigorous gasping and contraction of muscles around the neck, abdomen, buttocks and limbs.</li>
<li>In both males and female's anal sphincter contracts rhythmically</li>
<li>Contraction of the uterus in females</li>
<li>Muscle spasms occurs both in male and females</li>
<li>Blood pressure rises.</li>
<li>Heart rate rises</li>
<li>Respiration rate increases</li>
<li>It last for seconds to minutes</li>
</ul>
<p>IV. Resolution: This is the phase of muscular relaxation and the body system going back to its non sexual excitation state or baseline state.</p>
<ul>
<li>It last 10-15 minutes if orgasm is achieved.</li>
<li>It is characterized by:-</li>
<li>Disgorgement of blood from genitals (detumescence)</li>
<li>Male are physiologically refractory to further erection and orgasm for a variable period of time. (Males are unable to initiate further orgasm until after some times)</li>
<li>Females may respond to additional stimulation almost immediately.</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; Descending of the testes.
&gt; Muscular relaxation
&gt; General well being.
If orgasm was not achieved, the individual may present with:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Irritability</li>
<li>Discomfort</li>
<li>Prolonged resolution for hours</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sexual-disorders">Sexual disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sexual-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sexual disorders are problem with sexual response that causes a person mental distress or intense sexual behaviour that involves unusual situations.</p>
<p>It is disturbance in the process that characterizes sexual response cycle.</p>
<p>Occurrence of sexual dysfunction disorders can be grouped depending on:</p>
<p>a) Onset can be :</p>
<ul>
<li>Primary(lifelong)</li>
<li>Secondary (acquired)</li>
</ul>
<p>b) Context in which the dysfunction occurs</p>
<ul>
<li>Generalised-any time and any place</li>
<li>Situational-occurs in particular situations and places.</li>
<li>Lack of sexuality stimulating behaviour.</li>
</ul>
<p>c) Aetiological factors</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Psychological factors eg</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cognitive interference –negativism about sex</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fear of failure</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lack of communication by the factors</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Organic and Biological causes .eg</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Chronic diseases such as DM, sickle cell disease etc</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Congenital anomalies of the reproductive system</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cultural and religion factors</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Upbringing where sex topics are not supposed to be discussed</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prior learning-things learnt that affect sexual behaviour</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Religious teachings against sex and sex before marriage</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cultural values and norms relating to sex.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sexual disorders are classified into three major types:-
I. Sexual dysfunctions
II. Gender identity disorder.
III. paraphilias</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sexual-dysfunction-disorders">Sexual dysfunction disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sexual-dysfunction-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>I. Sexual desire disorders</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<ul>
<li>Hypoactive sexual desire disorder</li>
<li>Sexual aversion disorder.</li>
</ul>
<p>II. Sexual arousal disorder</p>
<ul>
<li>Female sexual arousal disorder</li>
<li>Male erectile disorder.</li>
</ul>
<p>III. Orgasmic disorders</p>
<ul>
<li>Female orgasmic disorder</li>
<li>Male orgasmic disorder</li>
<li>Premature ejaculation</li>
</ul>
<p>IV. Sexual pain disorders</p>
<ul>
<li>Dyspareunia</li>
<li>Vaginismus.</li>
</ul>
<p>V. Sexual disorder due to a general medical condition
VI. Substance induced sexual disorder
VII. Sexual disorder NOS (Not Otherwise Specified)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hypoactive-sexual-desire-disorder">Hypoactive sexual desire disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypoactive-sexual-desire-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is reduced or lack of interest in sexual activity. It is manifested as:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Inhibited sexual desire</li>
<li>Low sexual desire</li>
<li>Deficient/ absent sexual fantasies and libido</li>
<li>The individual avoid arousing situations</li>
<li>Develops rapid turn off</li>
<li>Complains of Poor or lack of response by the partner</li>
<li>Anxiety and guilt may be manifested</li>
<li>Specify the type either 1°,2° etc.</li>
<li>Common in females than in males</li>
<li>Causes difficulties in marital relationship</li>
</ul>
<p>♦ Causes of Hypoactive sexual desire disorder:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Organic causes</li>
<li>Biological causes</li>
<li>Psychological causes</li>
<li>Cultural and religion factors</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sexual-aversion-disorder">Sexual aversion disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sexual-aversion-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is persistent or recurrent extreme aversion to or avoidance of all or almost all genital sexual contact with a sexual partner</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>Sexual aversion disorder can be primary and secondary types</p>
<ul>
<li>In primary type the genital sexual contact has never been experienced</li>
<li>In secondary type genital sexual contact has been experienced before.</li>
</ul>
<p>It can also assume situational type in which genital sexual contact is possible with different partner and in different settings and it is more common in women than in men.</p>
<p>When confronted with the sexual situation the person may experience:</p>
<ul>
<li>Panic attacks</li>
<li>Extreme anxiety</li>
<li>Feeling of terror</li>
<li>Faintness</li>
<li>Nausea</li>
<li>Vomiting</li>
<li>Palpitations</li>
<li>Dizziness</li>
<li>Dyspnoea.</li>
</ul>
<p>Persons with this disorder have impaired relationships</p>
<p>They tend to avoid sexual situations or potential partners by covert strategies such as:</p>
<ul>
<li>Going to sleep early</li>
<li>Travelling</li>
<li>Neglecting self appearance</li>
<li>Involving in substance use</li>
<li>Being over involved in other activities e.g. Work or school</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aetiology-of-sexual-aversion-disorder">Aetiology of sexual aversion disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aetiology-of-sexual-aversion-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A. Psychological factors-sexual traumatic experiences, sexual abuse etc
B. Cognitive aspect-low self esteem, hostile feelings towards the partner, fear of pregnancy, marital conflicts, affective disorders.
C. Certain organic causes- diabetes mellitus, hypertension, neurological diseases, liver diseases, gynaecological cancers, pharmacological agents e.g. antihypertensives, diuretics, TCAs, alcohol etc, nutritional deficiencies e.g. Vitamin A, zinc.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="female-sexual-arousal-disorder">Female sexual arousal disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#female-sexual-arousal-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is inability to attain or maintain until completion of the sexual activity an adequate lubrication-swelling response.</p>
<p>It is characterized by:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Lack of response to sexual stimulation in females.</li>
<li>Failure to acquire adequate lubrication during sexual activity.</li>
</ul>
<p>It has two main causes:</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<ul>
<li>Subjective –feeling of no arousal</li>
<li>Physiological –lack or failure of vaginal lubrication</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="male-erectile-disorder">Male erectile disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#male-erectile-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It is persistent or recurrent inability to attain or maintain until completion of the sexual activity an adequate erection.</li>
<li>It also referred to as:</li>
<li>Erectile dysfunction</li>
<li>Inhibited sexual excitement</li>
<li>Impotence</li>
<li>It can assume different patterns such as:</li>
<li>Not able to attain an erection at all</li>
<li>Erection may be achieved during masturbation.</li>
<li>It can either be:</li>
<li><strong>Primary</strong> erectile dysfunction where by an individual has never achieved an erection</li>
<li><strong>Secondary</strong>-the individual has ever had adequate erection but unable to achieve one in subsequent sexual encounters.</li>
<li>Associated causes or etiology of male erectile disorder include:-</li>
<li>Sexual anxiety i.e. fear of failure</li>
<li>Decreased sense of sexual pleasure</li>
<li>Infertility</li>
<li>Depression</li>
<li>Perceived loss of physical appearance</li>
<li>Poor communication between partners.</li>
<li>Hostile attitude by the partner</li>
<li>In adequate sexual information</li>
<li>mistrust</li>
<li>Substance use</li>
<li>Severe stress</li>
<li>Fear of pregnancy</li>
<li>Traumatic sexual experience</li>
<li>Religion factors</li>
<li>Restrictive upbringing</li>
<li>Organic disorders such as diabetes, circulatory heart diseases.</li>
<li>Hormonal imbalance</li>
<li>Neurological disorders</li>
<li>Some medications</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="female-orgasmic-disorder">Female orgasmic disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#female-orgasmic-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>It is persistent or recurrent delay in or absence of orgasm following a normal sexual excitement phase.</li>
<li>It can either be:</li>
<li>a. Primary-the person has never reached orgasm</li>
<li>b. Secondary-the person may have reached orgasm in the past.</li>
<li>The person may experience orgasm in some certain circumstances e.g. When fantasising about sexual encounter.</li>
<li>Also known as:</li>
<li>Orgasmic dysfunction</li>
<li>Anorgasmia</li>
<li>Inhibited female orgasm</li>
<li>Causes of female orgasmic:</li>
<li>Fear of pregnancy</li>
<li>Depression</li>
<li>Poor sexual techniques.</li>
<li>Passivity due to cultural and religion rules</li>
<li>Lack of affection</li>
<li>Sexual boredom</li>
<li>Aversion towards the partner</li>
<li>Disturbed interpersonal relationship</li>
<li>Marital conflict</li>
<li>Poor sexual communication</li>
<li>Lack of interest in sexual activity</li>
<li>Depression/ Stress</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="male-orgasmic-disorder">Male orgasmic disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#male-orgasmic-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>It is persistent or recurrent delay in or absence of orgasm following a normal sexual excitement phase.</li>
<li>Also known as:</li>
<li>a. Retarded ejaculation</li>
<li>b. Inhibited male orgasm</li>
<li>Causes:</li>
<li>a. Depression</li>
<li>b. Poor sexual techniques</li>
<li>c. Passivity due to cultural and religion rules</li>
<li>d. Lack of affection</li>
<li>e. Sexual boredom</li>
<li>f. Aversion towards the partner</li>
<li>g. Disturbed interpersonal relationship</li>
<li>h. Marital conflict</li>
<li>i. Poor sexual communication</li>
<li>j. Lack of interest in sexual activity</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>k. Depression/Stress</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="premature-ejaculation">Premature ejaculation.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#premature-ejaculation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It is persistent or recurrent ejaculation with minimal sexual stimulation on or shortly after penetration and before the person wishes it.</li>
<li>Aetiology/causes:</li>
<li>Factor that affects Duration of the excitement phase e.g. Age, frequency and duration of coitus.</li>
<li>Fear of being watched or discovered by others especially when sex is performed illegally or takes place in inappropriate places and situation.</li>
<li>Negative attitude towards the female partner</li>
<li>Focus on achieving an orgasm</li>
<li>Hostility by the partner</li>
<li>Inexperience</li>
<li>Environmental stress.</li>
<li>Organic causes:</li>
<li>Urethral disorders</li>
<li>Neurological disorders</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vaginismus">Vaginismus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vaginismus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It is recurrent or persistent involuntary spasm of the musculature of the outer third of the vagina that interferes with sexual intercourse.</li>
<li>It may occur prior to or during penetration</li>
<li>Penile penetration become impossible when there is contraction of the pelvic floor muscles to the extent that the vagina does not dilate.</li>
<li>Extreme cases of Vaginismus may lead to non-consummation of marriage.</li>
<li>Vaginismus is often psychogenic in origin.</li>
<li>It is triggered by fear of penetration, pregnancy or contracting disease.</li>
<li>Other causes may include:</li>
<li>Hostility and traumatic sexual experience</li>
<li>Strong religious belief.</li>
<li>Organic causes:</li>
<li>Gynaecological lesions</li>
<li>Inflammation</li>
<li>Obstetric trauma</li>
<li>Hymenal remnants</li>
<li>Atrophy of the vagina in senile women.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dyspareunia">Dyspareunia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dyspareunia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It is recurrent or persistent pain associated with sexual intercourse in either male or female.</li>
<li>Dyspareunia may be an indication of inadequate vaginal lubrication possibly due to insufficient stimulation.</li>
<li>Other factors:</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<ul>
<li>Lesions, scars, muscle spasm</li>
<li>Effects of circumcision e.g. tight circumcision, formation of fibrous tissue.</li>
<li>Pelvic infection on deep penetration</li>
<li>Inflammation</li>
<li>Ca cervix</li>
<li>Ovarian cysts</li>
<li>Penile infection in men</li>
<li>Structural abnormalities in male genitalia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="gender-identity-disorder">Gender identity disorder.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gender-identity-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A strong and persistent cross-gender identification that is not merely a desire for any perceived cultural advantages of being the other gender.</li>
<li><strong>Transexualism:</strong> It is a disorder where the person has the conviction of being sex opposite to that indicated by the external genitalia.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="paraphilias">Paraphilias.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#paraphilias" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Paraphilias are unusual fantasies, sexual urges and behaviours that are recurrent and arousing.</li>
<li>They include:</li>
<li>a) <strong>Paedophilia</strong>-sexual urge towards arousal or activity with a pre-pubescent child</li>
<li>b) <strong>Exhibitionism</strong>- exposure of genitalia by a male to unsuspecting female stranger which may be accompanied by a fantasy that the stranger will be sexually aroused</li>
<li>c) <strong>Fetishism</strong>-use of women’s underpants, bras, stockings, shoes, earings, bracelets among others for the purpose of achieving sexual arousal and gratification.</li>
<li>d) <strong>Transvestism</strong>-recurrent act of cross-dressing, usually by heterosexual male in female dressing for the purpose of achieving sexual arousal and gratification.</li>
<li>e) <strong>Sexual masochism</strong>-seeking of real humiliation or pain from physical injuries or psychological abuse in order to achieve sexual gratification. e.g.. Beating, being tied, stabbing, cutting, receiving electrical shock, piercing or psychological abuse before or during sexual intercourse.</li>
<li>f) <strong>Sexual sadism</strong>-derives sexual excitement from physical and psychological suffering and humiliations of their victims</li>
<li>g) Paraphilias NOS(Not Otherwise Classified):</li>
<li>Zoophilia/Bestialism: an animal</li>
<li>Telephone scatologia: obscene phone calls</li>
<li>Necrophilia: corpses</li>
<li>Partialism: exclusive focus on one part of the body</li>
<li>Coprophilia: feaces</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<ul>
<li>Klismaphilias: enemas</li>
<li>Urophilia: urine</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-sexual-disorders">Management of sexual disorders: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-sexual-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Conduct a comprehensive assessment on the following key aspects:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The nature and development of the sexual problem</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Family attitudes towards sexuality – "taboo" element</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sexual knowledge: how and from where was it gained</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Gender identity and role: did the individual feel safe with the gender identity or role during childhood or adolescent</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Puberty: when did this occur, was it early or late compared with peers, was it traumatic, for the female; ask about the onset and early understanding of menstruation and subsequent patterns.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Interest in opposite sex: when did it develop and what was the nature of the first heterosexual relationship?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Past sexual experiences</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Current relationships: when did the couple meet; what attracted them to each other and how did the relationship develop</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Assess for any medical conditions (e.g. diabetes, neurological diseases, pelvic pathology, medicines) or psychiatric factors (mood and anxiety disorders) that could account for the problem.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Psychological intervention</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Counselling – to allay myths, improving love making techniques and communication.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Behavioural therapies – marital therapy, sensate focus (focussing on other areas other than sex organs to reduce sex performance anxiety)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sensate focus: involves exploration of each other’s bodies in order to give and receive pleasurable sensations with emphasis on communication and giving pleasure in order to receive it. Sensate focus is meditation about sexual affairs.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Genital sensate focus: the couple move to involve the genital and breast areas in their caressing and exploration.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Squeeze techniques – a method commonly used to treat premature ejaculation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In this technique, the female partner holds the male’s sexual organ between her thumb and forefinger at the level of the frenulum</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When the male partner is about to ejaculate he signals his partner to tightly apply squeeze technique by squeezing the tip of the male organ</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The procedure is slightly painful and should be practiced for a while until male partner do not ejaculate too soon.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Stop-start techniques – manual stimulation of the man’s sexual organ. When the male partner is about to have an ejaculation he informs the partner to apply start-stop technique.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Manage underlying medical conditions</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cognitive and social interventions – self-instruction training</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Other therapies</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>✓ Individual therapy.
✓ Group therapy
✓ aversion therapies
✓ Negative Sex thinking.
✓ Positive sex thinking e.g. visualizing a past episode of a prolonged sexual activity.
✓ Non sexual thinking and practice- eg expressing gratitude for one another, Having dinner together etc.
✓ Sex incongruous.
✓ Drugs e.g. Sildenafil (Viagra)</p>
<p>You can also Adopt Annon's PLISSIT model</p>
<ul>
<li>P-Permission: -This is when you seek permission from the client to discuss feelings and concerns relating to specific health issues they are hesitant to discuss</li>
<li>LI-Limited Information: This is the second stage where the therapist offers basic education about the topic at hand.</li>
<li>SS-Specific Suggestions: This level of intervention involves advanced knowledge of a particular health issue and develop an appropriate interventional plan</li>
<li>IT: Intensive Therapy: This is the fourth level of intervention and it requires specialized and intensive interventional program.</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC
20</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="youth-and-adolescent-reproductive-health">Youth and adolescent reproductive health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#youth-and-adolescent-reproductive-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="learning-objectives">Learning objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#learning-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>By the end of the lesson the learner should be able to:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Define terminologies related to youth and adolescent reproductive health.</li>
<li>Define adolescent, youth and young people.</li>
<li>Outline changes that occurs during puberty and adolescent.</li>
<li>Explain rationale for focussing on adolescent and youth reproductive health</li>
<li>Describe youth friendly services</li>
<li>Outline roles of health service providers in adolescent and youth reproductive health.</li>
<li>Discuss barriers to youth and adolescent reproductive health services.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>During this transition to adulthood, adolescents develop biologically and psychologically and move towards independence and due to these transitional changes, youths and adolescents:</p>
<ul>
<li>Encounter health risks</li>
<li>Exhibit risk taking behavior</li>
<li>Experimental risk behavior</li>
</ul>
<p>According to world health organization (WHO): -</p>
<ul>
<li>Adolescence - refers to the period of life between the ages of 10 and 19 years.</li>
<li>Youth - refers to the period of life between the ages of 15 and 24 years.</li>
<li>Young people - refers to the period of life between the ages of 10 and 24 years.</li>
<li>Teenager - persons aged 13-19 yrs</li>
</ul>
<p>Social definition of adolescence: This is the stage in human development covering the onset of puberty until full social integration of the individual as an adult. This is a period in which an individual goes through physical and psychological changes accompanied by sexual maturation leading to the capacity to procreate.</p>
<p>Biological Definition of adolescence: This is a period in which an individual goes through physical and psychological changes accompanied by sexual maturation leading to the capacity to procreate.</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="stages-of-adolescence-development">Stages of adolescence development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stages-of-adolescence-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Adolescence stage can be divided into three:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Early adolescence</li>
<li>Middle adolescence</li>
<li>Late adolescence.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="early-adolescence-10-13yrs">Early adolescence (10-13yrs)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#early-adolescence-10-13yrs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Onset of puberty and rapid growth</li>
<li>Impulsive, experimental behavior</li>
<li>Beginning to think abstractly</li>
<li>Adolescent’s sphere of influence extends beyond her/his own family</li>
<li>Increasing concern with image and acceptance by peers</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="middle-adolescence-14-16-yrs">Middle adolescence (14-16 yrs)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#middle-adolescence-14-16-yrs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Continues physical growth and development</li>
<li>Starts to challenge rules and test limits</li>
<li>Develops more analytical skills; greater awareness of behavioral consequences</li>
<li>Strongly influenced by peers, especially on image and social behavior</li>
<li>Increasing interest in sex; special relationships begin with opposite sex</li>
<li>Greater willingness to assess own beliefs and consider others</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="late-adolescence-17-19-yrs">Late adolescence (17-19 yrs)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#late-adolescence-17-19-yrs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Reaches physical and sexual maturity.</li>
<li>Improved problem-solving abilities</li>
<li>Developing greater self-identification</li>
<li>Peer influence lessens</li>
<li>Reintegration into family</li>
<li>Intimate relationships more important than group relationships</li>
<li>Increased ability to make adult choices and assume adult responsibilities</li>
<li>Movement into vocational life phase</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="puberty">Puberty<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#puberty" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Puberty is the period in which individuals acquire sexual maturity.</li>
<li>It occurs between 11-13 years.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="physiological-and-physical-changes-that-occurs-during-puberty">Physiological and Physical changes that occurs during puberty<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physiological-and-physical-changes-that-occurs-during-puberty" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>This is going to be discussed based on girls and boys</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="girls">Girls<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#girls" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Breasts increase in size and are spherical in shape due to enlarged glandular tissue</li>
<li>Typical female shape and contour of the body develop, that is broad hips and narrow chest and shoulders</li>
<li>Hair develops in the armpits and pubic region</li>
<li>Internal organs of reproduction, that is, vagina, uterus, ovaries mature and menstruation (menarche) begins</li>
</ul>
<p>Face may become smooth or facial pimples (acne) may develop</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="boys">Boys<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#boys" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Enlarged testis and penis</li>
<li>Development of armpit, pubic and facial hairs</li>
<li>First ejaculation (spermache) and nocturnal emissions (wet dreams) occur</li>
<li>Gain in muscular strength and weight</li>
<li>Voice changes with the voice becoming deeper</li>
<li>Skin problems such as acne develop and the face looks rough</li>
<li>Body shape takes on typical adult characteristics, for example, broad shoulders</li>
<li>Rapid growth in height depending on genetics</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="emotional-and-psychological-changes-in-adolescence">Emotional and psychological changes in adolescence<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#emotional-and-psychological-changes-in-adolescence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Changing relationships with parents, which may involve the adolescent pulling away and becoming more independent</li>
<li>Changing relationships with friends. Adolescents often imitate the values and behaviors of friends rather than those of parents and other adults. Peers are an important influence but they care more about what their friends think of them. This is called peer influence.</li>
<li>The relationship with the opposite sex increases as they learn how to cope with romantic and sexual feelings. This is the period of sexual debut for many adolescents.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Sexual Debut</strong> is the age at which and individual engages in his/her first sexual intercourse.</p>
<ul>
<li>Personal feelings are also affected and there is a need to accept themselves as an independent individual</li>
