<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pre-conception-care-delivery-areas">PRE CONCEPTION CARE DELIVERY AREAS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pre-conception-care-delivery-areas" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>It is important that these services are not stand alone, but are rather integrated into other services and programmes; such as: Family planning services, Antenatal care services, Child welfare clinic, Postpartum care, Outpatient services, Youth friendly sites, Comprehensive care clinics, Specialized clinics, School health programmes, VCT centres, and other specific service sites that target men</li>
<li>Creating linkages with other disciplines to promote pre-conception care</li>
<li>Create awareness for other professionals e.g.,</li>
<li>Physicians to educate diabetics, cardiac patients, and others with medical conditions; pediatricians; nutritionist etc.</li>
<li>Community awareness and participation</li>
<li>Schools, Women’s groups, Public barazas, faith based institutions, youth clubs, etc.</li>
<li>Linkages with other programmes (HIV, Child health, vaccines), Other sectors / Ministries (Education, Gender, Agriculture, Culture and Social services) and other stakeholders</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="community-midwifery">Community midwifery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-midwifery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="learning-objectives">Learning objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#learning-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>By the end of the lesson the learner should be able to:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Define terminologies related to community midwifery</li>
<li>Describe the theory of three delays</li>
<li>Outline aims of community midwifery</li>
<li>Describe health care organization in Kenya</li>
<li>State services offered in community midwifery services</li>
<li>Outline roles and duties of community midwives</li>
<li>Describe the process of recruiting and selection of community midwifery service providers</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Community midwifery was developed to close the gap that exists among women on childbirth by a skilled birth attendant.</li>
<li>The community midwifery model ensures that skilled care is available during pregnancy, labour and child birth and follow-up of both mother and baby postnatally in the community.</li>
<li>The Community Midwifery Model (CMM) uses skilled attendants out of work or retired licensed health care professionals who are resident within a given community and seeks to contribute towards improvement of reproductive health.</li>
<li>Community midwifery model seeks to support the provision of equitable, accessible, affordable and quality health and related services at the highest attainable standards to all Kenyans using the primary health care approach.</li>
<li>Community midwifery model is a key strategy in ensuring that women access adequate reproductive health services from a skilled birth attendant.</li>
<li><strong>Definition of Community</strong>: It is a specific group of people, often living in a defined geographical area, who share a common culture, values, and norms and who are arranged in a social structure according to relationships the community has developed over a period of time.</li>
<li><strong>Definition of community midwifery</strong>: It is the care given by a skilled birth attendant to childbearing women during the process of childbirth, labour and postnatal in the community or at home.</li>
<li><strong>Skilled Birth Attendant' (SBA)</strong> is defined as “an accredited health professional such as a midwife, doctor or nurse who has been educated and trained to proficiency in the skills needed to manage normal (uncomplicated) pregnancies, childbirth and the immediate postnatal period, and in identification, management and referral of complications in women and newborns”</li>
<li><strong>Definition of a midwife</strong>: A midwife is a person who, having been regularly admitted to a midwifery educational program that is duly recognized in the country in which it is located, has successfully completed the prescribed course of studies in</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>midwifery and has acquired the requisite qualifications to be registered and/or legally licensed to practice midwifery.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Reasons that have been found to contribute to home deliveries includes:-</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lack of privacy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Long distance to health facilities</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>High cost of healthcare services</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Uncooperative health staff</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Theory of the ‘3’ delays:-</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>1st delay- Delay at home</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>2nd delay- Delay in reaching a health facility</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>3rd delay-Delay at the hospital</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>1st delay:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>First delay is the delay that occurs at home. The mother delays from seeking health care as a result of home related reasons. These factors may include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lack of funds to seek health care</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cultural factors that prohibit use of health services</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Religious factors that prohibit use of health services</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lack of knowledge to recognize danger signs/symptoms</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>2nd delay:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This is the delay that occurs in reaching a health. This may include</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Poor road network</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lack of means of transport</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sparsely located health facilities</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Delay in referral between various health facilities</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>3rd delay:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This is the delay that occurs within a health facility. It may include:-</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lack of services</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Shortage of staff</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Long waiting time</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hospital beurocracy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Health care provider’s attitude</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Shortage of supplies</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Aims/ objectives of community midwifery:-</p>
<ul>
<li>To make reproductive more accessible to the community</li>
<li>To reduce maternal mortality rate and neonatal mortality rate.</li>
<li>To increase utilization for reproductive health services by the community members.</li>
<li>To promote community involvement in maternal and newborn care.</li>
<li>To provide basic emergency obstetric and newborn care within the community.</li>
<li>To promote childbearing by a skilled birth attendant.</li>
<li>To create link between the community and the formal health system in matters relating to reproductive health</li>
</ul>
<p>Current organization of health care system in Kenya: -</p>
<ul>
<li>The current system is organized into four tiers, namely:-</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<ul>
<li>TIER I: Community level: The foundation of the service delivery system, with both demand creation and specified supply services that are effectively delivered at the community.</li>
<li>TIER II: Primary care level: The first physical level of the health system, comprising all dispensaries, health centres &amp; maternity /nursing homes. It is the 1st care level, where most clients' health needs should be addressed.</li>
<li>TIER III: County level: The first level hospitals, whose services complement the primary care level to allow for a more comprehensive package of services.</li>
<li>TIER IV: National level: The tertiary level hospitals, whose services are highly specialized.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="services-offered-at-community-level">Services offered at community level:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#services-offered-at-community-level" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Immunization services</li>
<li>Child health</li>
<li>Maternal and newborn health</li>
<li>Screening for diseases</li>
<li>Water and Sanitation,</li>
<li>Provision of basic curative care</li>
<li>Prevention of HIV/STIs</li>
<li>Family planning among others</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="providers-of-health-services-at-the-community-level">Providers of health services at the community level:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#providers-of-health-services-at-the-community-level" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Community Health Workers (CHWs)</li>
<li>Community Health Extension Workers (CHEWs)</li>
<li>Community Midwives.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="criteria-for-selecting-community-midwifery-service-providers">Criteria for selecting community midwifery service providers:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#criteria-for-selecting-community-midwifery-service-providers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>In selection of potential candidates for community midwifery services, the following core qualifications are mandatory:
I. A health professional with evidence of one of the following qualifications:</li>
<li>☑ Registered Nurse/ Midwife; Enrolled Nurse/ Midwife Registered</li>
<li>☑ Clinical Officer</li>
<li>☑ Medical officer</li>
</ul>
<p>NB- Should be verified with the relevant professional body
II. A retired or out of employment health professional with obstetric/midwifery skills.
III. Has residency within the community to be served.
IV. Evidence of retention on a professional register (Nursing Council of Kenya, Kenya)
V. Clinical Officers' Council, the Medical Practitioners and Dentist Board)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="other-selection-criteria">Other selection criteria:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-selection-criteria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Get involved in the running of health related or welfare activities within the community as a sign of the community's trust in them</li>
<li>Be ready to be supervised and monitored by the county Health Management</li>
<li>Be ready for Training and Supervision by the county Teams ( RH Coordinators)</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>Be able to Link with the health care system through the nearest health facility for support such as updates, transport, supplies, equipment and their sterilization
Be willing to work closely with the community leaders and community groups to identify the most common health problems and work together for a solution.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="roles-and-responsibilities-of-community-midwife">Roles and responsibilities of community midwife:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#roles-and-responsibilities-of-community-midwife" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>I. Providing reproductive health care to women and their family members
II. Serving as a link between level I and the formal health system
III. Data collection and reporting</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="i-providing-reproductive-health-care-to-women-and-their-family-members">I. Providing reproductive health care to women and their family members<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#i-providing-reproductive-health-care-to-women-and-their-family-members" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Provision of information and education on preconception care and early initiation of antenatal care to women.</li>
<li>Provision of information on the importance of when and where to seek health care services during pregnancy, labour and childbirth and the postnatal period for mother and baby.</li>
<li>Provision of information on importance of testing for HIV and referral for HCT and PMTCT.</li>
<li>Educating women and their families on the importance of an individualized birth preparedness and postnatal plan.</li>
<li>Assisting a woman and her family to prepare a birth, postnatal care plan including postpartum family planning.</li>
<li>Educating women on the identification of danger signs in pregnancy labour, childbirth and postnatal period.</li>
<li>Educating women on how to recognize danger signs in the newborn including sepsis to ensure family seeks early treatment</li>
<li>Provision of reproductive health knowledge among women and their male partners.</li>
<li>Provision of information on the importance of breastfeeding.</li>
<li>Provision of information on the availability of family planning commodities.</li>
<li>Educating women on the importance of completing immunization schedules for infants/children and TT schedule for women.</li>
<li>Monitoring of pregnancy through FANC</li>
<li>Following up with the link facility to ensure that antenatal profile is done</li>
<li>Provision of targeted postnatal care to women</li>
<li>Supporting HIV care including ART adherence, opportunistic infections management and linkages to HIV support centres and local support groups</li>
<li>Counseling women on exclusive breast feeding and Lactational Amenorrhoea Method (LAM) as well as on broader aspects of nutritional counseling.</li>
<li>Provision of minor curative services as defined in the community health strategy.</li>
<li>Referral of clients to health facilities for laboratory tests, immunizations, etc</li>
<li>Receiving referrals from community health workers for further management.</li>
<li>Coordination of activities with the health extension workers and community health committees</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>The role of community midwives includes the initial appointments with pregnant women, managing clinics, postnatal care in the home, and attending home births.</p>
<p>A community midwife would typically have a pager and be responsible for a particular area, contacted by ambulance control when needed. Sometimes they are paged to help out in the hospital when there are insufficient midwives available.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ii-serving-as-a-link-between-level-i-and-the-formal-health-system">II. Serving as a link between level I and the formal health system:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ii-serving-as-a-link-between-level-i-and-the-formal-health-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Community midwife works closely with community Health extension workers (CHEWs) and community health workers (CHWs) in delivery of maternal and newborn health interventions at the community.</li>
<li>The community midwife is expected to link with other players at the community level as well as formal health system.</li>
<li>Community midwife is also required to establish a regular contact with various teams at community level.</li>
<li>Community midwife should create links with local health committees.</li>
<li>The community midwife will act an advisor to the local health committees on maternal and newborn health issues.</li>
<li>The main functions of local health committee are:-</li>
<li>Resource mobilization</li>
<li>Providing support to community reproductive activities</li>
<li>Educating households on matters pertaining to reproductive health issues.</li>
<li>providing leadership support for safe pregnancy and childbirth</li>
<li>Facilitating the acquisition of key infrastructure for community health workers and community midwives.</li>
<li>Providing security to community midwives.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-health-facilities-links-with-community-midwives">How health facilities links with community midwives:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-health-facilities-links-with-community-midwives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The health facility in-charges and the facility management teams supported by the county and sub-county authorities should provide support to the community midwife</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ways-through-which-health-facilities-can-support-community-midwives">Ways through which health facilities can support community midwives:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ways-through-which-health-facilities-can-support-community-midwives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Overseeing the performance of the community midwife and other extension workers</li>
<li>Supplying the community midwife with drugs, equipment and other supplies for safe delivery</li>
<li>Facilitating referral of clients (or women) with complications or other forms of emergency to static health facilities by availing transport.</li>
<li>Providing stationery or forms to the community midwife for monthly reports.</li>
<li>Strengthening infection prevention and control efforts e.g. In the disposal of sharps and sterilization of equipment, etc.</li>
<li>Organizing for in-service training/Continuing Professional Development, involving community midwives in relevant stakeholder meetings, seminars etc.</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>III. Link between a community midwife and a community health worker:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Community midwife should provide overall support to community health workers with a view to building their skills and knowledge in the core basic and technical components in reproductive health.</li>
<li>community midwife will equip the CHW with appropriate skills and knowledge to be able to:</li>
<li>Advise on items required for the delivery</li>
<li>Assist the woman and her family to identify somebody to assist her after childbirth</li>
<li>Advise family to look out for danger signs in mother and baby</li>
<li>Advise the mother/family to register the baby’s birth with the local administration</li>
<li>Advise on taking baby to health facility for immunizations and growth monitoring and women for postnatal care</li>
<li>Map where all pregnant and newly delivered women live</li>
<li>Encourage the woman’s family to provide social support in pregnancy/ postnatal period</li>
<li>Report on any deaths of mothers and infants in the community including any stillbirths</li>
</ul>
<p>Data collection and compiling reports: -</p>
<ul>
<li>A community midwife should be able to:</li>
<li>☑ Compile data, write and submit reports to the local health management teams and committees promptly.</li>
<li>☑ Register or advise the woman on where to register the birth</li>
<li>☑ Notify the civil registration office/health facility of any death in the community</li>
<li>☑ Share monthly reports with the link health facility using the appropriate register(s) document(s) from the ministry of health. The report should include; Number of women assisted during childbirth; Number registered for birth certification; Number of Stillbirths (FSB and MSB) and any maternal deaths.</li>
<li>☑ Document the number of referrals; reasons for referral for both mother and</li>
<li>☑ newborn; means of transport used; source of funds for transport; person accompanying patient and the outcome of the referral process (if known).</li>
</ul>
<p>Scope of practice: -</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The Community midwives scope of practice is:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Preconception care counseling</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Normal pregnancy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Childbirth, postpartum</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ New born care and</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Family planning.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Community</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>NB:</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<ul>
<li>midwives will practice within the guidelines and protocols developed by regulating bodies.</li>
<li>Referral care should be provided in case of emergency</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="training-of-community-midwives-in-kenya">Training of community midwives in Kenya:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#training-of-community-midwives-in-kenya" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>According to Community Midwifery Services in Kenya: Implementation Guidelines; Second Edition of August 2012 stipulates that although midwives at retirement, resignation or departure are qualified and experienced, the environment they start working as community midwives is different.</li>
<li>Therefore this guidelines recommends that those who want to become community midwives should complete the following steps:-</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Orientation</li>
<li>Clinical attachment in a busy health facility for skills updates.</li>
<li>Certification and</li>
<li>Licensing.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="orientation">Orientation:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#orientation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The orientation will focus on the following core skills:</li>
<li>Maternal and newborn care</li>
<li>Maternal and perinatal death surveillance and response.</li>
<li>Recording and reporting data.</li>
<li>Infection prevention and control</li>
<li>Family planning</li>
<li>communication and referral</li>
<li>Entrepreneurship and marketing skills</li>
<li>Interpersonal and communication skills.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-attachment-in-a-busy-health-facility-for-skills-updates">Clinical attachment in a busy health facility for skills updates:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-attachment-in-a-busy-health-facility-for-skills-updates" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The practical attachment should be at a busy health facility where there is a high client load and a range of maternal and newborn health care services provided.</li>
<li>The community midwife should be provided with a log book to record required procedures which should be carried out under supervision</li>
<li>Areas to cover in clinical placement include:-</li>
<li>In ANC Clinic</li>
<li>Understand focused antenatal care (diseases prevention and health promotion, IBP)</li>
<li>Participate in Health talks</li>
<li>Head to toe examination including palpations to identify the gestation, lie, presentation and position</li>
<li>Breast examination</li>
<li>TT immunisation, heamatinics, IPT for malaria ITN</li>
<li>PMTCT</li>
<li>Assist 5 women prepare an individualized birth and postnatal plan</li>
<li>Record all procedures in the appropriate documents (ANC card and registers)</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="labour-and-delivery">Labour and delivery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#labour-and-delivery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Admit women in labour (history taking)</li>
<li>Manage labour using a partograph</li>
<li>PMTCT</li>
<li>Assist mothers during childbirth (10)</li>
<li>Active management of third stage of labour (AMTSL)</li>
<li>Manual removal of retained placenta</li>
<li>Suturing of any simple tears or episiostomy</li>
<li>Record all procedures in the appropriate documents (delivery, PNC, ANC card)</li>
<li>Familiarize with the data collecting tools</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="postnatal">Postnatal:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#postnatal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Carry out complete postnatal check on mother before leaving hospital</li>
<li>Carry out complete postnatal check on the baby before discharge</li>
<li>PMTCT care and follow-up (know where to refer CCC/support groups etc)</li>
<li>Record all procedures on appropriate documents (ANC/PNC card and register)</li>
<li>Postnatal check at 14 days</li>
<li>Postnatal check at 6 weeks</li>
<li>Family planning advice - LAM and transition to other methods</li>
<li>Breastfeeding support</li>
<li>Essential newborn care - specifically in nursery</li>
<li>Health education/counsel the woman eg on danger signs for both mother and newborn</li>
<li>Immunisations /child welfare clinic</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="documents">Documents<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#documents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Monthly summary reporting fo</li>
<li>Patients case notes</li>
<li>Referral forms</li>
<li>Partographs</li>
<li>Maternity Register</li>
<li>Post natal register</li>
<li>Mother Child Health Booklet</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="certification-and-licensing">Certification and licensing:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#certification-and-licensing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Once the Community Midwife has satisfactorily completed all the procedures outlined in the log book, they will be certified by the Ministry of Health. A regulatory body such as the (Nursing Council of Kenya or its equivalent) will then issue a license to the health provider to practice in the community</li>
<li>The community midwives will be required to have relevant regular updates and refresher courses in order to meet requirements for retention.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principles-of-community-midwifery">Principles of community midwifery:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-community-midwifery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Community participation</li>
<li>Resource mobilization</li>
</ul>
<p>47</p>
<ul>
<li>Effective community organization</li>
<li>Effective community leadership</li>
<li>Effective monitoring and supervision strategies</li>
<li>Awareness creation and consensus building.</li>
<li>Intersectoral collaboration.</li>
<li>Effective health management information system</li>
<li>Sustainability</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-to-make-community-midwifery-effective">How to make community midwifery effective: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-to-make-community-midwifery-effective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>For effective community midwifery there should be: -</li>
<li>☑ identification and recruitment of Community Midwives</li>
<li>☑ Identification potential local facilitators to conduct updates and on-job training for CMs</li>
<li>☑ Facilitate training of trainers for Community Midwives</li>
<li>☑ Train Community Midwives according to guidelines</li>
<li>☑ Register all Community Midwives working in the district</li>
<li>☑ Ensure all Community Midwives have the appropriate licensing documents</li>
<li>☑ Compile monitoring data and produce periodic reports</li>
<li>☑ Facilitate collaboration with stakeholders and secure resources for the program</li>
<li>☑ Coordinate on-going support supervision</li>
<li>☑ Ensure re-supply of consumables through facilities and or District stores,</li>
<li>☑ Support supervision</li>
<li>☑ Details for communication set up</li>
<li>☑ Referral mechanisms for emergencies agreed with VHC and HF Management Boards</li>
<li>☑ Organizing capacity building and CPD/in-service training</li>
<li>☑ Identify sources of supplies, equipment and essential drugs</li>
<li>☑ Provide Community Midwife with necessary equipment</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="community-midwifery-financing">Community midwifery financing:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-midwifery-financing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Government (treasury allocations)</li>
<li>Health sector services Fund(HSSF)</li>
<li>Output based aid(OBA)</li>
<li>Direct budgetary allocation to community units.</li>
<li>Private financing</li>
<li>National hospital insurance fund(NHIF)</li>
<li>Support from development partners</li>
<li>Donations from charity organizations.</li>
<li>Leveraging from local development funds eg CDF.</li>
</ul>
