<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="maternal-mortality-and-maternal-death-reviews">Maternal mortality and maternal death reviews<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maternal-mortality-and-maternal-death-reviews" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="learning-objectives">Learning objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#learning-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>By the end of the lesson the learner should be able to:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Define terminologies related to maternal mortality and death reviews</li>
<li>Outline causes of maternal deaths</li>
<li>State factors influencing perinatal mortality.</li>
<li>List ways of preventing perinatal deaths</li>
<li>Describe approaches to maternal deaths surveillance and response.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="definition-of-terms">Definition of terms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition-of-terms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li><strong>Maternal death /mortality</strong>: It is the death of a woman while pregnant or within 42 days of the termination of pregnancy irrespective of the duration and the site of the pregnancy, from any cause related to or aggravated by the pregnancy or its management but not from accidental or incidental causes.</li>
<li><strong>Maternal mortality ratio</strong>: It is the number of maternal deaths per 100,000 live births. The current maternal mortality ratio in Kenya is 362/100,000 live births.</li>
<li><strong>Perinatal mortality/death</strong>: It is foetal deaths after 28 weeks gestation and those occurring within the first 7 days after birth including still births.</li>
<li><strong>Perinatal Mortality Rate (PMR)</strong>: It is the number of perinatal deaths divided by the number of total births multiplied by 1000</li>
<li>The current perinatal rate is 22 deaths per 1,000 live births.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="factors-influencing-perinatal-mortality">Factors influencing perinatal mortality<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-influencing-perinatal-mortality" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Maternal age</li>
<li>Parity</li>
<li>Birth weight</li>
<li>Quality of management of labour and delivery</li>
<li>Mode of onset of labour</li>
<li>Duration of labour</li>
<li>Mode of delivery</li>
<li>Complications of labour in mature babies/newborns</li>
<li>Low Birth Weight</li>
<li>Infections</li>
<li>Congenital malformations</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-of-perinatal-deaths">Prevention of perinatal deaths<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-of-perinatal-deaths" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Active management of labour using the partograph and use of timely caesarean section</li>
<li>By appropriate antenatal care, including acceleration of lung maturity, screening for STIs</li>
<li>Appropriate neonatal resuscitation</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<ul>
<li>By careful preconception screening and counseling, screening (CVS, U/S, maternal serum and amniotic fluid alpha fetoprotein) and early termination of pregnancy.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes-of-maternal-deaths">Causes of maternal deaths<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-maternal-deaths" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Causes of maternal deaths is classified into two:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Direct causes</li>
<li>Indirect causes</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="direct-causes">Direct causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#direct-causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>These are deaths from complications of pregnancy, labour, and puerperium.</li>
<li>These causes include:</li>
<li>Ectopic pregnancy</li>
<li>Abortions</li>
<li>APH (Antepartum hemorrhage)</li>
<li>PPH (Postpartum hemorrhage)</li>
<li>Eclampsia</li>
<li>Ruptured uterus</li>
<li>Obstructed labour</li>
<li>Sepsis</li>
<li>Embolism</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indirect-causes">Indirect causes:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indirect-causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Indirect causes include:</li>
<li>HIV-AIDS</li>
<li>Anemia</li>
<li>Malaria</li>
<li>Cardiac diseases</li>
<li>Tuberculosis</li>
<li>Pneumonia</li>
<li>Diabetes</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maternal-deaths-review-maternal-audit">Maternal deaths review/maternal audit:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maternal-deaths-review-maternal-audit" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A maternal death audit is an in-depth systematic review of maternal deaths to identify underlying health; social and other contributory factors to maternal death.</li>
<li>It also provides a learning opportunity as such audits are used in making recommendations to prevent similar deaths in future.</li>
<li>It is not a process for apportioning blame or shame but exists to identify and learn lessons from the remediable factors that might save the lives of more mothers in future.</li>
<li>MOH form 372 is used for maternal death review.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="importance-of-maternal-deaths-review-audit">Importance of maternal deaths review/ audit:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#importance-of-maternal-deaths-review-audit" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Provides ways of preventing future deaths</li>
<li>Provides an opportunity to evaluate health systems</li>
<li>Provides evidence based decision making process on the relevant interventions</li>
<li>It also provides evidence based resource allocation</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="approaches-in-reviewing-maternal-deaths-maternal-audit">Approaches in reviewing maternal deaths/ maternal audit:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#approaches-in-reviewing-maternal-deaths-maternal-audit" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>WHO has described five (5) approaches in maternal death review; namely:</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<ol>
<li>Facility-based maternal death review</li>
<li>Community-based maternal death review (verbal autopsy)</li>
<li>Confidential enquiries into maternal deaths</li>
<li>Survey of severe morbidity (near misses)</li>
<li>Clinical audit</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="facility-based-maternal-death-review">Facility-based maternal death review<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#facility-based-maternal-death-review" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It is an in-depth investigation of the causes of and associated factors in maternal deaths that occur in</li>
<li>It entails interviews of health personnel who attended to the deceased.</li>
<li>It can also be extended to members who accompanied the deceased.</li>
<li>The review is nonjudgmental to encourage the cooperation of the health workers involved.</li>
<li>It provides information for improving obstetric care.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="community-based-maternal-death-review-verbal-autopsy">Community-based maternal death review (verbal autopsy)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-based-maternal-death-review-verbal-autopsy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It is in-depth nonjudgmental investigation of the causes and the associated factors of maternal deaths that occur outside health facilities.</li>
<li>It entails interviews of family members who cared for the deceased.</li>
<li>This requires a community informant to let local authorities know whenever there is a death of a reproductive-age female in the community.</li>
<li>The interviewer, who is usually not a health worker, should be sensitive when probing the circumstances leading to the death. In some cultures, the interview is done after the mourning period.</li>
<li>A team of health care workers then examines the interview notes to determine the cause of death.</li>
<li>When this is combined with the facility-based review described above, it gives a more complete picture of maternal deaths in a given local jurisdiction.</li>
<li>MOH form 519 is used in verbal autopsy.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="confidential-enquiries-into-maternal-deaths">Confidential enquiries into maternal deaths:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#confidential-enquiries-into-maternal-deaths" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A national or sub-national multidisciplinary committee meets periodically to systematically investigate a representative sample of (or all) maternal deaths to identify the causes and associated factors.</li>
<li>The committee gives written guidelines to health personnel and administrators on how to prevent similar deaths in future.</li>
<li>The investigation is carried out in a confidential manner ("No blame, no shame").</li>
<li>The files are recalled to a central unit where anonymization process takes place.</li>
<li>It requires a complete and functioning civil registration or health management information system.</li>
<li>A sub national or sub-county -level panel might be more appropriate in countries with high mortality, so that the guidelines issued can be tailored to local situations.</li>
<li>Facilitating steps in confidential maternal review include: -</li>
<li>An adequate legal framework</li>
<li>A clear and systematic way of retrieving files</li>
<li>A more efficient process for anonymizing case notes</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<ul>
<li>Improved quality of data</li>
<li>Improved capacity to accurately identify the underlying cause of death</li>
<li>Surveillance of maternal deaths</li>
<li>Remedial action</li>
<li>Sustained source of funding</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="survey-of-severe-morbidity-near-misses">Survey of severe morbidity (near misses)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#survey-of-severe-morbidity-near-misses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A near-miss event refers to one in which a woman has nearly died but survived a complication that occurred during pregnancy, childbirth, or within 42 days of termination of pregnancy.</li>
<li>This survey is an in-depth investigation of the factors that led to the near miss, what worked well in the treatment of the life-threatening complications, and the lessons learned.</li>
<li>Unlike the other approaches, in this one the pregnant woman herself is also interviewed, creating the opportunity to obtain more insight into the circumstances.</li>
<li>This survey is less threatening to health personnel than the others, since the women have survived.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-audit">Clinical audit<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-audit" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>This entails a systematic review or audit of the obstetric care provided to pregnant women against established protocols or criteria aimed at improving the quality of care.</li>
<li>Protocols for the management of obstetric complications will have to be established beforehand in order to ascertain whether cases are properly being managed at health facilities.</li>
<li>If well implemented, it leads to standardized and improved care across health facilities.</li>
</ul>
<p>NB: Maternal Death review should be conducted within 7 days after occurrence of death in case of facility based review and 30 days for community based review.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maternal-death-notification">Maternal death notification<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maternal-death-notification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Notification is the process of issuing a formal message officially.</li>
<li>Maternal death that occurs within the facility should be notified within 24 hours</li>
<li>Maternal death that occurs within the community should be notified within 48 days.</li>
<li>The notification is made through filling form MOH 370</li>
<li>The form provides information on the following:</li>
<li>Locality where the death occurred</li>
<li>Details of the deceased</li>
<li>Details of admissions</li>
<li>Underlying cause of death.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maternal-death-surveillance-and-response-mdsr">Maternal death surveillance and response (MDSR)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maternal-death-surveillance-and-response-mdsr" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It is a continuous cycle of identification, notification and review of maternal deaths followed by actions to improve quality of care and prevent future maternal deaths.</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="key-components-of-a-national-maternal-death-surveillance-and-response-mdsr-system">Key Components of a National Maternal Death Surveillance and Response (MDSR) System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#key-components-of-a-national-maternal-death-surveillance-and-response-mdsr-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A national policy to notify all maternal deaths</li>
<li>A national policy to review all maternal deaths</li>
<li>A national maternal death review committee in place</li>
<li>Sub national maternal death review committees in place</li>
<li>Both national and sub national maternal death review committees in place</li>
<li>A national maternal death review committee that meets at least biannually.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principles-of-mdsr">Principles of MDSR:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-mdsr" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Notification within 24 hours of maternal deaths in facilities (or within 48 hours when a woman dies in the community)</li>
<li>Zero reporting when no suspected maternal deaths have occurred</li>
<li>Timely review of all probable maternal deaths</li>
<li>Immediate recommendations, where possible, to help facilities and communities prevent similar deaths, ensuring that key messages reach people who can make a difference</li>
<li>Timely review and analysis at county and national levels to identify trends and patterns Timely publication of findings and recommendations at national level</li>
<li>Continuous monitoring of the MDSR system and of how recommendations are implemented</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="general-functions-of-maternal-death-surveillance-and-review-include">General functions of maternal death surveillance and review include:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-functions-of-maternal-death-surveillance-and-review-include" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Review all maternal deaths at health facilities.</li>
<li>Ensure that the recommendations issuing from committee meetings are followed through to improve obstetric services;</li>
<li>Report the findings (without personal identifying information) to the higher-level committee(s)—Sub county, county, or national and the civil registration system.</li>
<li>Provide feedback to lower-level committees;</li>
<li>Share aggregate statistics with the HIMS</li>
<li>Provide input into any future revisions of the audit forms and guidelines.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="assignment">ASSIGNMENT:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assignment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Each student to read and write short notes on</p>
<p>a) Various committees at different levels</p>
<p>b) Advantages and disadvantages of each maternal review approach</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="safe-motherhood-maternal-and-newborn-health">Safe motherhood/Maternal and Newborn Health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#safe-motherhood-maternal-and-newborn-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="learning-objectives">Learning objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#learning-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>By the end of the lesson the learner should be able to: -</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Define safe motherhood</li>
<li>Outline objectives of safe motherhood</li>
<li>State principles of safe motherhood</li>
<li>List challenges facing safe motherhood</li>
<li>Discuss pillars of safe motherhood</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The concept of maternal and newborn health (MNH) is now being used to refer to safe motherhood.</li>
<li>Safe motherhood is an approach of ensuring that women have access and ability to have safe and healthy pregnancy and delivery.</li>
<li>Making motherhood safe requires action on three key areas:</li>
<li>Reduce the number of high risk and unwanted pregnancies</li>
<li>Reduce the number of obstetric complications</li>
<li>Reduce the cases of high fertility rate in women with complications</li>
<li>Strategies that are required to achieve safe motherhood initiative include:-</li>
<li>Improving availability of maternal and newborn health</li>
<li>Increasing access to maternal and newborn health</li>
<li>Increasing utilization of quality maternal and newborn health.</li>
<li>Reducing unmet family planning needs for women</li>
<li>Strengthening referral system</li>
<li>Advocating for increased commitment and resources for MNH</li>
<li>Promoting and strengthening community based MNH</li>
<li>Strengthening monitoring and evaluation for MNH</li>
<li>The Kenya MNH model recognizes the potential role communities have in the promotion of their own health including that of maternal and newborn health.</li>
<li>It reiterates the importance of strengthening the interface between the community and health services, as well as promoting the human rights approach to health service delivery.</li>
<li>For effective maternal and newborn health, the following should be ensured:-</li>
<li>Ensuring training and deploying of adequate number of skilled health workers to provide antenatal, intrapartum and postnatal care.</li>
<li>Creating enabling environment for health care workers including infrastructural advancement</li>
<li>Effective coordination of MNH services</li>
<li>Promotion of quality MNH services</li>
<li>Establishing effective referral system</li>
<li>Promoting community involvement and partnership</li>
<li>Ensuring equity for all</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<ul>
<li>Advocating and maintaining reproductive health for mothers and newborns.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="challenges-facing-mnh">Challenges facing MNH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#challenges-facing-mnh" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Limited availability of MNH services</li>
<li>Shortage of staff trained on MNH</li>
<li>Low basic emergency and newborn care coverage.</li>
<li>Lack of community involvement in MNH</li>
<li>Limited national commitment and resources for MNH</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives-of-mnh-include">Objectives of MNH include:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives-of-mnh-include" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>To increase the availability, accessibility, acceptability and utilization of skilled birth attendance during pregnancy, child birth and postnatal period at all levels of health care delivery system.</li>
<li>To strengthen the capacities of individuals, families, communities and social networks to improve maternal and newborn health.</li>
<li>To strengthen data management and utilization for improved MNH</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pillars-of-safe-motherhood-maternal-and-newborn-health">Pillars of safe motherhood/ maternal and newborn health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pillars-of-safe-motherhood-maternal-and-newborn-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Family planning and pre-pregnancy care – To ensure that individuals and couples have the information and services to plan the timing, number and spacing of pregnancies.</li>
<li>Focused Antenatal Care – To prevent complications where possible and ensure that complications of pregnancy are detected early and treated appropriately.</li>
<li>Essential Obstetric Care – To ensure that essential care for the high-risk pregnancies and complications is made available to all women who need it.</li>
<li>Essential Newborn Care – To ensure that essential care is given to newborns from the time they are born up to 28 days in order to prevent complications that may arise after birth.</li>
<li>Targeted Postpartum Care – To prevent any complication occurring after childbirth and ensure that both mother and baby are healthy and there is no transmission of infection from mother to child.</li>
<li>Post Abortion Care – to provide clinical treatment to all women and girls seeking care, for complications of incomplete abortion and miscarriage as well as counseling and contraceptives.</li>
<li>Clean and Safe Delivery: This ensures that birth attendants have the knowledge, skills, positive attitude and equipment to perform a clean and safe delivery and provide postpartum care to the mother and baby.</li>
<li>Prevention of Mother to Child Transmission of HIV (PMTCT): These are measures and interventions that are put in place to ensure little or no transmission of HIV virus from the mother to the baby.</li>
</ol>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anatomy-and-physiology-of-reproductive-system">Anatomy and Physiology of Reproductive system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anatomy-and-physiology-of-reproductive-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="learning-objectives">Learning objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#learning-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>By the end of the lesson the learner should be able to: -</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Describe main structures of male and female external genitalia.</li>
<li>Describe major structures of male and female internal genitalia</li>
<li>Discuss spermatogenesis and oogenesis.</li>
<li>Explain the process of ejaculation in males</li>
<li>Explain the reproductive cycle in females</li>
<li>Describe the structure and functions of female breast</li>
<li>Outline types of nipples</li>
<li>Explain the physiology of lactation</li>
<li>Describe structure and function of female pelvis.</li>
<li>Describe foetal skull.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Reproductive system and structures are adapted to propagate new individuals and for continuation of human species.</li>
<li>Organs that are specialized for production of male and female sex cells are called gonads.</li>
<li>The male gametes are called spermatozoa and female gametes are called ova.</li>
<li>Gonads produces both gametes secrete and sex hormones</li>
<li>Male gonads are the testes and female gonads are the ovaries.</li>
<li>Males and females produce specialized reproductive germ cells known as gametes.</li>
<li>Sex cells are referred to as gametes and they are the ones that creates genetic variation</li>
<li>Reproductive system is made up of the following structures</li>
<li>Gonads, ducts, glands &amp; supporting structures</li>
<li>Chromosome passes inherited characteristics on to the next generation.</li>
<li>Gametes contain only 23 chromosomes whereas other body cells contain 46 chromosomes.</li>
<li>Gametes are formed through meiosis.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="male-reproductive-system">Male reproductive system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#male-reproductive-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Male reproductive system is classified as:-</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>External male reproductive system</li>
<li>Internal reproductive system.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="external-male-reproductive-system">External male reproductive system.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#external-male-reproductive-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The structures that forms external male reproductive system include:-</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Scrotum</li>
<li>Penis</li>
</ol>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-scrotum">1. Scrotum<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-scrotum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Scrotum is Sac of loose skin, fascia &amp; smooth muscle divided into two pouches by a septum.</li>
<li>It is made up of deeply pigmented skin fibrous connective tissue &amp; smooth muscle.</li>
<li>Each compartment of the scrotum contains:</li>
<li>a) One testes</li>
<li>b) One epididymis</li>
<li>c) One testicular end of a spermatic cord</li>
<li>Scrotum lies below symphysis pubis in front of upper part of thighs and behind pelvis</li>
<li>The cremaster muscle draws the testes closer to the body when it is too cold, and lowers the testes away from the body when it is too warm.</li>
<li>Cremasteric reflex is contraction of the cremaster muscle, in response to the stroking of the thigh.</li>
<li>Sperm production and survival requires 2-3 degrees' lower temperature than core body temperature</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="functions-of-the-scrotum">Functions of the scrotum<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-the-scrotum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>a) Contains and protects the testes.</li>
<li>b) Regulate temperature less than body temperature for the purpose of spermatogenesis</li>
<li>c) Contracts to bring the testes close to the body when temp are cold and vice versa</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="layers-of-the-scrotum">Layers of the scrotum<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#layers-of-the-scrotum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Layers of the scrotum include:-</li>
<li>a) The skin</li>
<li>b) Superficial 'Dartos' fascia</li>
<li>c) External spermatic fascia</li>
<li>d) Cremaster muscle and fascia</li>
<li>e) Internal spermatic fascia</li>
<li>f) Parietal layer of tunica vaginalis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="blood-supply-to-the-scrotum">Blood supply to the scrotum<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#blood-supply-to-the-scrotum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Scrotum receives arterial blood supply from:-</li>
<li>a) Anterior scrotal artery</li>
<li>b) Posterior scrotal artery</li>
<li>Anterior scrotal artery is a branch of external pudendal artery</li>
<li>Posterior scrotal artery arises from internal pudendal artery</li>
<li>The scrotal venous drainage is through scrotal veins that runs along major arteries and drains into external pudendal veins</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="innervations-of-the-scrotum">Innervations of the scrotum<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#innervations-of-the-scrotum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Innervations of the scrotum is derived from the following nerves:</li>
<li>a) Genital branch of genitofemoral nerve - Derived from the femoral plexus and supplies the anterolateral aspect of the scrotum</li>
<li>b) Anterior scrotal nerves - They are derived from ilioinguinal nerve and supplies the anterior aspect of the scrotum.</li>
</ul>
<p>c) Posterior scrotal nerves-They are derived from the perineal nerve and supplies the posterior aspect of the scrotum.
d) Perineal branches of posterior femoral cutaneous nerve-Derived from the sacral plexus and supplies the inferior aspect of the scrotum.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lymphatic-drainage">Lymphatic drainage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lymphatic-drainage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The lymph system of the scrotum drains into the superficial inguinal nodes.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-344fe550.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-penis">2. Penis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-penis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Penis: a cylindrical-shaped male organ made of specialized erectile spongy tissue that erects upon sexual arousal.
Its reproductive purpose is as a conduit for semen (and sperm).
The head of the penis or glans contains many nerve endings and is covered by a loosely fitting skin called the foreskin.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span>  Tumescence is the engorgement of penile blood vessels leading to an erection.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span>  Detumescence is the process in which the blood leaves the penile tissue leading to its flaccid state.
At tip penis is expanded into triangular structure i.e. glans penis.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span>  Above glans, skin is folded upon itself to form a movable double layer foreskin or prepuce
The penis is composed of three cylinders, containing sponge-like erectile tissue to cause an erection.</p>
<p>I. Corpora cavernosa- two cylinders lie on the upper sides of the penis.
II. Corpus spongiosum- central cylinder lies on the bottom and contains the urethra.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span>  Penis has two (dual) states:</p>
<p>a) Flaccid
b) Erect</p>
<p>It has two (dual) functions</p>
<p>a) Expulsion (passage) of urine
b) Expulsion (passage) of semen</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span>  Penis is anatomically made of three parts, namely:-</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-the-root">a) The root<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-the-root" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  it is the most proximal, fixed part of the penis. It is located in the superficial perineal pouch of the pelvic floor.
It is not visible externally.
The root contains three erectile tissues (two crura and bulb of the penis), and two muscles (ischiocavernosus and bulbospongiosus).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="b-the-shaft-body">b) The shaft(body)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-the-shaft-body" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The free part of the penis, located between the root and glans.
It is suspended from the pubic symphysis.
It is composed of three cylinders of erectile tissue - two corpus cavernosa, and the corpus spongiosum.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="c-glans-penis">c) Glans penis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-glans-penis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The most distal part of the penis.
It is conical in shape, and is formed by the distal expansion of the corpus spongiosum.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  This contains the opening of the urethra, termed the external urethral orifice (external urethral meatus).
It has dense concentration of nerve endings making it highly sensitive.</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-b98a56be.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg"></p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="vasculature-of-the-penis">Vasculature of the penis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vasculature-of-the-penis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Arterial blood supply to the penis is derived from three main sources: -</li>
<li>a) Dorsal arteries of the penis</li>
<li>b) Deep arteries of the penis</li>
<li>c) Bulbourethral artery</li>
<li>&gt; NB: These arteries are branches of common penile artery (internal pudendal artery).</li>
<li>Venous blood is drained from the penis by two veins.</li>
<li>a) The cavernous spaces are drained by the deep dorsal vein of the penis – This empties into the prostatic venous plexus.</li>
<li>b) The superficial dorsal veins supply the superficial structures of the penis, such as the skin and cutaneous tissues.</li>
<li>&gt; NB: These veins eventually drains into internal pudendal and internal iliac veins</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-d385c6b4.jpeg" alt="img-4.jpeg"></p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="innervations-of-the-penis">Innervations of the penis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#innervations-of-the-penis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Nervous supply to penis is by autonomic and somatic nerves.</li>
<li>The penis is supplied by S2-S4 spinal cord segments and spinal ganglia.</li>
<li>Sensory and sympathetic innervation to the skin and glans penis is supplied by the dorsal nerve of the penis, a branch of the pudendal nerve.</li>
<li>Parasympathetic innervation is carried by cavernous nerves from the prostatic nerve plexus, and is responsible for the vascular changes which cause erection.</li>
<li>Sympathetic innervation is responsible for ejaculation.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ligaments">Ligaments<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ligaments" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The root of the penis is supported by two ligaments, which attach it to the surrounding structures:</li>
<li>a) <strong>Suspensory ligament</strong> – It is the condensation of deep fascia. It connects the erectile bodies of the penis to the pubic symphysis.</li>
<li>b) <strong>Fundiform ligament</strong> – It is the condensation of abdominal subcutaneous tissue. It runs down from the linea alba, surrounding the penis like a sling, and attaching to the pubic symphysis.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="skin-of-the-penis">Skin of the penis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#skin-of-the-penis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The skin of the penis is more heavily pigmented than that of the rest of the body.</li>
<li>It is connected to the underlying tunica albuginea by loose connective tissue.</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>The prepuce (foreskin) is a double layer of skin and fascia, located at the neck of the glans. It covers the glans to a variable extent.
The prepuce is connected to the skin of the glans by the frenulum, a median fold of skin on the ventral surface of the penis.
The potential space between the glans and prepuce is termed the preputial sac.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="internal-structures-organs-of-male-reproductive-system">Internal structures/organs of male reproductive system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#internal-structures-organs-of-male-reproductive-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-testes">1. Testes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-testes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Testes are reproductive glands of the male equivalent of the ovaries in female.</li>
<li>They are suspended in scrotum by the spermatic cords.</li>
<li>Testes are surrounded by three layers of tissue:-</li>
<li>a) Tunica vaginalis</li>
<li>b) Tunica albuginea</li>
<li>c) Tunica vasculosa</li>
<li>Tunica Vaginalis—this is a double membrane forming the outer covering of testes and it is the down growth of the abdominal and pelvic peritoneum.</li>
<li>Tunica albuginea—this is the fibrous covering beneath tunica vaginalis. It is the one that divides the glandular structure of the testes into lobules.</li>
<li>Tunica vasculosa—this consists of a network of capillaries supported by delicate connective tissue</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="anatomical-structure-of-testes">Anatomical Structure of testes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anatomical-structure-of-testes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Each testis has about 200-300 lobules.</li>
<li>Each testis is about 4.5 cm long 2.5 cm wide and 3 cm thick.</li>
<li>It is suspended by spermatic cord in the scrotum.</li>
<li>Each lobule has 1-4 convoluted loops composed of germinal epithelia cells called seminiferous tubules.</li>
<li>Seminiferous tubules contain: -</li>
<li>a) Sperm forming cells</li>
<li>b) Sertoli cells (supporting cells)</li>
<li>Sertoli cells extend from basement membrane to lumen of seminiferous tubules.</li>
<li>The functions of sertoli cells include: -</li>
<li>a) Forms blood-testis barrier</li>
<li>b) Support developing sperm cells through nourishment.</li>
<li>c) Produce fluid &amp; control release of sperm into lumen</li>
<li>d) Secretory Function—Secretes various proteins that are key in spermatogenesis such as: inhibin which slows sperm production; Adrogen Binding protein that binds testosterone; Activins that stimulates spermatogenesis</li>
<li>e) Phagocytosis—Sertoli cells engulfs and consumes unwanted elements during spermatogenesis</li>
<li>f) Immunological functions—Sertoli cells ensures that pathogens from the blood and other sources are not able to destroy the developing sperms</li>
<li>Between the seminiferous tubules are interstitial cells (of Leydig) that secrete testosterone.</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<ul>
<li>At the upper part of the testes, the tubules combine to form a single tubule. This tubule is called the <strong>epididymis</strong> and leaves the scrotum as <strong>deferent duct</strong> (Vas deferens) in the spermatic cord.</li>
<li>Blood and lymph vessels pass to the testes in the spermatic cord.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-2a5851ed.jpeg" alt="img-9.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-e33955a5.jpeg" alt="img-10.jpeg"></p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="functions-of-the-testes">Functions of the testes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-the-testes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Manufactures spermatozoa in seminiferous tubules.</li>
<li>Stores sperms in the epididymis.</li>
<li>Initiates motility of sperms during ejaculation</li>
<li>It has endocrine Function-Synthesis of testosterone.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vasculature-of-the-testes">Vasculature of the testes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vasculature-of-the-testes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Arterial blood supply to the testes and epididymis is through:</li>
<li>Paired testicular arteries that runs through the spermatic cord</li>
<li>Venous drainage is via paired testicular veins that run through the spermatic cord.</li>
<li>☑ Testicular veins are network of veins that are coiled around the testicular artery. This is known as pampiniform plexus</li>
<li>☑ Left testicular vein drains into the left renal vein while right testicular vein drains directly into inferior vena cava.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lymphatic-system-of-the-testes">Lymphatic system of the testes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lymphatic-system-of-the-testes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Lymphatic drainage of the testes is through lumbar and para-aortic lymph nodes which are located L1 of the vertebrae.</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="innervation-to-the-testes">Innervation to the testes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#innervation-to-the-testes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Testes are supplied by the genital branch of genitofemoral nerve and testicular nerves that form the sympathetic nerve supply.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-spermatic-cord">2. Spermatic cord<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-spermatic-cord" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It is a cord-like structure in males that runs from the deep inguinal ring down to each of the testes.</li>
<li>It suspends the testes in the scrotum.</li>
<li>This cord extends through the inguinal canal and attached to the testes on the posterior wall.</li>
<li>Spermatic cord is surrounded (covered) by three layers of tissues; namely: -</li>
<li>a) External spermatic fascia</li>
<li>b) Cremasteric muscle</li>
<li>c) Internal spermatic fascia</li>
<li>Each cord contains (content of spermatic cord)</li>
<li>a) Arteries: Testicular artery, cremasteric artery and deferential artery.</li>
<li>b) Testicular veins (Pampiniform plexus)</li>
<li>c) Lymph vessels</li>
<li>d) Vas Deferens (deferent duct)</li>
<li>e) Testicular (autonomic nerves) and genitofemoral nerve</li>
<li>f) Processus vaginalis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-epididymis">3. Epididymis:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-epididymis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It is a tubular, coiled structure within the scrotum attached to the backside of each testis.</li>
<li>It serves to store, mature, and transport sperm between the testes and the vas deferens.</li>
<li>Epididymis is made up of three parts:</li>
<li>a) The head - It is located on superior pole of testis. It stores sperms for maturation</li>
<li>b) The body - It connects the head to the tail of the epididymis. It is the portion of sperm maturation</li>
<li>c) The tail - The tail of the epididymis is continuous with the deferent duct.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-vas-deferens">4. Vas Deferens:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-vas-deferens" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>These are two long, thin tubes that lead from the epididymis to the seminal vesicles and prostate gland.</li>
<li>Also known as ductus deferens</li>
<li>The contraction of the vas deferens during ejaculation pushes the sperm out.</li>
<li>Vas deferens forms a conduit for sperms during ejaculation into the ejaculatory duct.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-ejaculatory-duct">5. Ejaculatory duct:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-ejaculatory-duct" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Ejaculatory is a tubular pathway that is formed from the union of vas deferens and the seminal vesicle ducts.</li>
<li>Ejaculatory ducts pass through the prostate gland and empties semen into the urethra during ejaculation.</li>
<li>It helps in combining sperms from vas deferens with secretions from the seminal vesicles.</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>After mixing of the sperms and fluid from seminal vesicle, this content then passes through the ejaculatory duct where it mixes further with the content from the prostate gland. The content of then drains into prostatic urethra.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-seminal-vesicles">6. Seminal Vesicles:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-seminal-vesicles" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>These are two vascular glands lying behind the bladder with ducts joining the vas deferens.</li>
<li>They are located posteriorly and inferiorly to the urinary bladder and lateral to vas deferens.</li>
<li>The excretory ducts of the seminal vesicles join with the vas deferens to form ejaculatory duct.</li>
<li>They secrete a sticky fluid (constituting 70% of the semen) that nourishes and enables the sperm to move.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-prostate-gland">7. Prostate Gland:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-prostate-gland" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>This a doughnut-shaped gland with two lobes.</li>
<li>It is located in below the bladder and about half between rectum and the base of the penis.</li>
<li>It lies below the seminal vesicles and surrounds the urethra at the base of the bladder.</li>
<li>It stores and secretes an alkaline fluid that neutralizes acid found in the male urethra and the female reproductive tract. Without the secretions of the prostate gland, many sperm would die and fertilization of an ovum would be impossible.</li>
<li>This fluid from prostate gland contains clotting enzyme that thickens the semen in the vagina.</li>
<li>The fluid also gives semen milky like appearance.</li>
<li>During ejaculation the smooth muscles of the prostate contract squeezing its content into the prostatic urethra and later expelled out as semen.</li>
<li>Functions of the prostate gland include:</li>
<li>a) Secrets thin milky fluid that makes up 30% of semen gives it milky appearance.</li>
<li>b) Contains clotting enzyme which thickens semen in the vagina increasing likelihood of semen being retained close to the cervix.</li>
<li>c) The fluid is alkaline in nature neutralizing acidic environment in the vagina.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ce0a3982">8. Cowper’s Gland:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ce0a3982" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>These are two small, pea-sized glands located beneath the prostate gland on both sides of the base of the penis.</li>
<li>They are situated in the deep perineal pouch.</li>
<li>Also known as bulbourethral glands.</li>
<li>They secrete a clear, sticky fluid (pre-ejaculation) that keeps the urethra moist.</li>
<li>It is alkaline to help neutralize the acidity of the urethra.</li>
<li>They are located below the prostate gland and at the origin of the internal part of the penis.</li>
<li>Secretions from these glands drain into the penile urethra.</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-diagram-showing-internal-structures-of-male-reproductive-system">A diagram showing internal structures of male reproductive system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-diagram-showing-internal-structures-of-male-reproductive-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-924b41bf.jpeg" alt="img-13.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="9-urethra">9. Urethra:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9-urethra" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Urethra is a pathway dual-purpose tube running the length of the penis from the bladder to the outside that transports both semen and urine.
The urethra in male provides a common pathway for the flow of urine and semen.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span>  Urethra is approximately 19-20 centimeters.
The male urethra consists of three parts: -</p>
<p>a) The prostatic Urethra-Originates at the urethral orifice of the bladder and passes through the prostate gland.
