b) The membranous urethra-originate from the prostate gland to the bulb of the penis. It is the shortest urethra.
c) Spongiose urethra/Penile Urethra-Lies within the corpus spongiosum of the penis and terminates at the external urethra orifice at glans penis</p>
<p>There are two urethral sphincters, namely: -</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-internal-urethral-sphincter">a) Internal urethral sphincter.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-internal-urethral-sphincter" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is formed between the urethra and the urinary bladder (At the neck of the bladder)
It is made up of smooth muscle and it is under involuntary control.
It is supplied by sympathetic nervous system which is a branch of autonomic nervous system.
During ejaculation it closes to prevent semen from draining into the urinary bladder (This phenomena of semen getting redirected to urinary bladder is called retrograde ejaculation)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="b-external-urethral-sphincter">b) External urethral sphincter<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-external-urethral-sphincter" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It made up of skeletal muscles and therefore it is under voluntary control.
It is located at the level of membranous urethra in males.
In females it is located at the distal inferior end of the bladder.
It is supplied and controlled by somatic nervous system.</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="10-sperm">10. Sperm:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#10-sperm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The male reproductive microscopic cell, produced by the testicles that can fertilize the female's ovum.</li>
<li>Sperm is a motile cell and is adapted for reaching and fertilizing the female ovum.</li>
<li>They are fertile for about 24-48 hours after being deposited into the female reproductive tract.</li>
<li>It is made up of three distinctive parts: -</li>
<li>a) The head – It contains DNA and the acrosome with enzymes for penetrating the ovum</li>
<li>b) The midpiece – It contains mitochondria to form ATP for energy</li>
<li>c) The Tail (flagellum) – It is used for locomotion</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-20292ac4.jpeg" alt="img-14.jpeg"></p>
<p>Diagrams showing structure (Morphology) of the sperm</p>
<p>The head of the sperm has acrosome that contains substances that assist in digesting the walls the ovum during fertilization. This will be discussed in details during topic on fertilization</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="spermatogenesis">Spermatogenesis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#spermatogenesis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Spermatogenesis is the physiological process of synthesizing and producing sperms in males.</li>
<li>Spermatogenesis occurs in the seminiferous tubules located within the testes.</li>
<li>Sperm formation occurs through meiosis that makes diploid cells into haploid sex cells.</li>
<li>Sperm forming cells undergoes two meiotic divisions:</li>
<li>a) First meiotic division</li>
<li>b) Second meiotic division</li>
<li>Spermatogonium is the undifferentiated germinal cell that eventually will differentiate into sperms.</li>
<li>Spermatogonium is a progenitor cell for spermatozoa.</li>
<li>Progenitor cell is a cell that has been committed to differentiate into sperm cell.</li>
<li>Spermatogonium (diploid cell) undergoes mitotic division to form daughter cell spermatogonium (diploid) that is pushed away from the basement membrane.</li>
<li>Daughter cell spermatogoniums further differentiate into primary spermatocyte with 46 chromosomes.</li>
<li>Primary spermatocyte undergoes first meiotic division to form two haploid secondary spermatocytes.</li>
<li>Secondary spermatocytes undergo second meiotic division to form four spermatids each with 23 single stranded chromosomes.</li>
<li>Each of the four spermatids will develop and mature into sperms.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-diagram-showing-spermatogenesis">A diagram showing spermatogenesis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-diagram-showing-spermatogenesis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-fa06deb1.jpeg" alt="img-15.jpeg"></p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>The spermatid later reorganizes itself to form a head, a midpiece, and a flagellum, or tail.</p>
<p>Cells involved in spermatogenesis include: -
a) Sertoli cells (nurse cells)
b) Leydig</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="erection-in-males">Erection in males<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#erection-in-males" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It occurs as a result of sexual stimulation
Erection in males is controlled by Parasympathetic nervous system reflex
Dilation of the arterioles supplying the penis makes more blood to enter the penis compressing the veins so that the blood is trapped.</p>
<p>This trapping of the blood within the penile vessels causes engorgement leading to an erection. This process is known as tumescence.</p>
<p>During resolution phase of sexual excitement, the penile arteries constricts decompressing the veins hence the penis becomes flaccid. (The penis goes back to non-erect state). This process is called detumescence.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="emission-and-ejaculation-in-males">Emission and Ejaculation in males<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#emission-and-ejaculation-in-males" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="emission">Emission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#emission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Muscle contractions close sphincter at base of bladder</li>
<li>Fluids are then propelled through ductus deferens, seminal vesicles, &amp; ejaculatory ducts into bulb of penis and mixes with prostatic fluid.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="ejaculation">Ejaculation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ejaculation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>It is controlled by sympathetic nervous system reflex</li>
<li>Skeletal muscles squeeze semen out through urethra</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hormonal-control-in-male-physiology">Hormonal control in male physiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hormonal-control-in-male-physiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Hypothalamus secretes gonadotropin releasing hormone (GnRH)
Anterior pituitary secretes FSH and LH
FSH causes Sertoli cells to secrete ABP and inhibin
LH causes interstitial cells to secrete testosterone
Testosterone: -</p>
<ul>
<li>stimulate spermatogenesis</li>
<li>Development and maintenance of male secondary sex characteristics.</li>
<li>inhibitory feedback on pituitary LH secretion</li>
<li>Exert protein-anabolic, growth promoting effect.</li>
</ul>
<p>It is controlled through negative feedback by an increase in testosterone and inhibin</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="semen">Semen:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#semen" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Semen is a mixture of sperms and seminal fluid</li>
<li>It is 60% from seminal vesicles and about 30% from prostate</li>
<li>It is slightly alkaline, milky appearance and sticky in nature</li>
<li>Semen contains nutrients, clotting proteins and an antibiotic to protect the sperms from injurious</li>
<li>A typical ejaculate is 2.5 to 5 ml in volume and a normal sperm count is 50 to 150 million/mL</li>
<li>Actions of many sperm are needed for one sperm to penetrate the ovum</li>
<li>If less than 20 million/mL the person is regarded as infertile.</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="female-reproductive-system">Female reproductive system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#female-reproductive-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Ovaries produce are adapted for production of eggs (oocytes) and hormones</li>
<li>Uterine tubes transport the eggs</li>
<li>Uterus is where fetal development occurs.</li>
<li>Female reproductive system is also made up of two structures/organs, namely: -</li>
<li>a) External genitalia (External reproductive structures)</li>
<li>b) Internal female genital organs (internal reproductive organs).</li>
<li>Vulva refers to all the structures that form the entire female external genitalia.</li>
<li>Vulva comes from a latin word that means "covering"</li>
<li>External genitalia are made up of the following: -</li>
<li>a) Mons Veneris/ Mons Pubis</li>
<li>b) Labia Majora</li>
<li>c) Labia Minora</li>
<li>d) Clitoris</li>
<li>e) Vestibule</li>
<li>f) Vaginal Opening</li>
<li>g) Urethral Opening</li>
<li>h) Hymen</li>
<li>i) Skene's Glands</li>
<li>j) Bartholin's Glands</li>
<li>k) Fourchette</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-mons-pubis">a. Mons pubis:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-mons-pubis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Mons pubis (Mons Veneris) is pad of adipose tissue located over the symphysis pubis (pubic bone joint)</li>
<li>Function: protects the junction of pubic bone from trauma</li>
<li>It is richly supplied with sebaceous glands</li>
<li>In childhood it is hairless and smooth</li>
<li>During puberty it is covered by a triangular coarse of curly hairs (escutcheon)</li>
<li>Pattern of hair growth:</li>
<li>☑ Female: Triangular</li>
<li>☑ Male: Diamond-shaped</li>
<li>Growth of pubic hair is stimulated by Testosterone while the pattern of hair growth is governed by estrogen.</li>
<li>The arterial blood supply to the mons pubis is from the inferior epigastric artery which is a branch of external iliac artery.</li>
<li>The lymphatic drains into the inguinal lymph nodes.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-labia-majora">b. Labia majora: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-labia-majora" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>These are two thick folds of adipose tissues originating from the mons pubis and terminating in the perineum.</li>
<li>It unites anteriorly to form the anterior commissure and posteriorly to form the posterior commissure.</li>
<li>Its outer surface is thick and covered by hair; inner surface is smooth and moist</li>
<li>Main function of the labia majora is to provide covering and protection to the external organs located under it.</li>
</ul>
<p>In nulliparous women: in close apposition to each other; but tends to gape wider after birth.
Two folds of skin running from the mons pubis to below the vaginal opening.
The area is rich in apocrine glands and sebaceous glands.
Labia majora arterial blood is from deep external pudendal artery.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span>  Nerve supply is from the perineal branch of posterior femoral cutaneous nerve.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="c-labia-minora">c. Labia minora:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-labia-minora" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>These are two thin fold of skin lying between labia majora.
It divides anteriorly to enclose the clitoris to form the prepuce.
Posteriorly labia minora fuse to form the fourchette.
It is most highly vascular, sensitive and richly supplied with sebaceous glands
In nulliparous women labia minora covers the vaginal introitus, vestibule and urethra</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="d-clitoris">d. Clitoris:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#d-clitoris" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is a small knob composed of erectile tissues and many sensitive nerve endings.
It is found above the opening of the vagina where the folds of the labia minora meet at the front.
It is homologous to the male penis.
It is regarded as the center of sexual sensation and stimulation in females.
highly sensitive and erectile tissue situated under the prepuce of the labia minora
Clitoris is covered by a fold of skin called prepuce; Sensitive to both touch and temperature
It is extremely sensitive and highly vascular and it plays part in orgasm of sexual intercourse. (female erogenous organ)
Clitoris is made up of three parts; namely:</p>
<p>a) Crura-Supports the exterior structures of the clitoris
b) Body-It is the cylindrical part of the clitoris containing erectile tissues. Extends from the clura and has blood vessels that when sexually aroused makes the clitoris to grow in size.
c) Glans-It is the pointed part of the clitoris that is highly sensitive.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="e-vestibule">e. Vestibule:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#e-vestibule" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is a triangular space between the labia minora where the following are located:</p>
<p>Urethral Opening (urethral meatus)
Vaginal Opening (vaginal introitus)
Opening of Bartholin's Glands
Opening of Skene's Glands</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="f-vaginal-opening">f. Vaginal opening:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#f-vaginal-opening" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It located between the opening of the urethra and the anus.
It is lined by outlets of Bartholin's Glands-They secretes mucus to lubricate vagina during sexual intercourse and its alkaline nature promotes sperm survival.
It is usually covered by a hymen in virginity
Hymen is thin and elastic semicircular membrane that covers the opening of the vagina. It is usually torn during the first sexual intercourse.</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span>  Imperforate Hymen - a hymen that completely covers the vaginal opening preventing coitus and passage of menstrual discharge</p>
<p>g. Skene's Gland-Located on each side of urethral opening and secretes fluid that also lubricate female genitalia during sexual intercourse.
h. Fourchette: It is the ridge of tissue formed by the posterior joining of the two labia minora and majora.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-4983dcc6.jpeg" alt="img-16.jpeg">
Diagram showing external female genitalia</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-e5528e4a.jpeg" alt="img-17.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-19be30f6.jpeg" alt="img-18.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="blood-supply-lymphatic-drainage-and-innervation-to-the-vulva">Blood supply, lymphatic drainage and innervation to the vulva<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#blood-supply-lymphatic-drainage-and-innervation-to-the-vulva" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Blood supply is via Internal and external pudendal artery and drainage through corresponding veins.</li>
<li>Lymphatic drainage is through inguinal glands.</li>
<li>Nerve supply is through branches of pudendal nerve. vaginal nerve supplies erectile tissue of vestibular bulb of clitoris.</li>
<li>Parasympathetic fibers have a vasodilator effect to the structures of the vulva.</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="internal-female-reproductive-organs">Internal female reproductive organs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#internal-female-reproductive-organs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Internal female reproductive organs include: -</li>
<li>a) Vagina</li>
<li>b) Cervix</li>
<li>c) Uterus</li>
<li>d) Fallopian tubes</li>
<li>e) Ovaries</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-vagina">a. Vagina:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-vagina" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Canal running from vestibule to the cervix passing upwards and backwards into the pelvis along a line approximately parallel to the plane of the pelvic brim.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It is approximately four-inch-long fibromuscular organ ending at cervix and lies between urinary bladder and rectum.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Vagina does not contain glands and it is moistened by mucus from cervix and other glands such as Bartholin's glands.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Vaginal fluid is strongly acid Ph of 4.5 due to presence of lactic acid formed by action of <em>doderleins bacillus</em> (are normal inhabitants of vagina).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Its walls are made up of skin folds known as rugae. Rugae appears at puberty and disappear at menopause.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rugae allows vaginal canal to stretch and enlarge during intercourse and delivery.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Functions of the vagina include: -</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Forms exit or escape of menstrual flow.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Receive penis and ejected sperms during sexual intercourse.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Provides passage for fetus during delivery.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Anatomical relation of the vagina.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Anterior-bladder and urethra. Closely connected to anterior vaginal</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Posterior – pouch of Douglas, rectum and perineal body</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Lateral – on either side of upper 2/3 are pelvic fascia and ureter pass beside the cervix, on either side of lower 1/3 are Ms. of pelvic floor</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Superior-uterus.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Inferior-external genitalia.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Blood supply to the vagina: Arterial supply is via branches of internal iliac artery and includes vaginal artery and a descending branch of uterine artery.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Venous supply is through corresponding veins.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lymphatic drainage – via inguinal, internal iliac and sacral glands.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nerve supply is from pelvic plexus.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>NB: Vaginal nerves follow vaginal arteries to supply vaginal walls and erectile tissue of the vulva.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-cervix">b. Cervix:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-cervix" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Cervix is the lower fibromuscular portion that joins with the uterus.</li>
<li>It is approximately 3-4 cm in length and 2.5 cm in diameter; however, it varies with age, parity and menstrual status.</li>
<li>It has three major parts; namely: -</li>
<li>☑ Internal os – is the narrow opening between isthmus and cervix. Isthmus is the junction between the cervix and the uterus. It is where squamocolumnar junction is located.</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><menclose notation="box"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="true"><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mstyle></mstyle></mstyle></menclose></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\boxed{\mathrm{C}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.3633em; vertical-align: -0.34em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 1.0233em;"><span style="top: -3.3633em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3.3633em;"></span><span class="boxpad"><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.0233em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3.3633em;"></span><span class="stretchy fbox" style="height: 1.3633em; border-style: solid; border-width: 0.04em;"></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.34em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> Cervical canal- A spindle-shaped tubular portion extending from the isthmus of the uterus to the opening of the uterus into the vagina
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><menclose notation="box"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="true"><mi mathvariant="normal">E</mi></mstyle></mstyle></mstyle></menclose></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\boxed{\mathrm{E}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.3633em; vertical-align: -0.34em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 1.0233em;"><span style="top: -3.3633em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3.3633em;"></span><span class="boxpad"><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">E</span></span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.0233em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3.3633em;"></span><span class="stretchy fbox" style="height: 1.3633em; border-style: solid; border-width: 0.04em;"></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.34em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> External os- is the opening at the lower end of the cervix. It is small and round before pregnancy, and becomes a transverse slit after pregnancy.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span> Cervix is joined to the uterus through isthmus.</p>
<p>c. Uterus:
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span> Uterus is the site of implantation and foetal development during pregnancy.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span> It is also a site for menstruation.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span> It is situated in the cavity of true pelvis behind bladder and in front of rectum.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span> It leans forward–anteversion and bends forwards on itself–anteflexion.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span> When woman is in standing position it results in almost horizontal position with fundus resting on the bladder.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span> Non-pregnant uterus is a hollow, muscular, pear shaped organ situated in the true pelvis.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span> Non pregnant uterus measures 7.5 cm long, 5cm wide and 2.5cm in depth, each wall being 1.25 cm thick.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span> Cervix forms lower 1/3 of the uterus and measures 2.5cm in direction.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span> The anatomical relation of the uterus is as follows: -
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><menclose notation="box"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="true"><mi mathvariant="normal">A</mi></mstyle></mstyle></mstyle></menclose></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\boxed{\mathrm{A}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.3633em; vertical-align: -0.34em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 1.0233em;"><span style="top: -3.3633em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3.3633em;"></span><span class="boxpad"><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">A</span></span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.0233em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3.3633em;"></span><span class="stretchy fbox" style="height: 1.3633em; border-style: solid; border-width: 0.04em;"></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.34em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> Anterior – uterovesical pouch and bladder.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><menclose notation="box"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="true"><mi mathvariant="normal">B</mi></mstyle></mstyle></mstyle></menclose></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\boxed{\mathrm{B}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.3633em; vertical-align: -0.34em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 1.0233em;"><span style="top: -3.3633em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3.3633em;"></span><span class="boxpad"><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">B</span></span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.0233em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3.3633em;"></span><span class="stretchy fbox" style="height: 1.3633em; border-style: solid; border-width: 0.04em;"></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.34em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> Posterior – recto uterine pouch of Douglas and rectum.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><menclose notation="box"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="true"><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mstyle></mstyle></mstyle></menclose></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\boxed{\mathrm{C}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.3633em; vertical-align: -0.34em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 1.0233em;"><span style="top: -3.3633em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3.3633em;"></span><span class="boxpad"><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.0233em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3.3633em;"></span><span class="stretchy fbox" style="height: 1.3633em; border-style: solid; border-width: 0.04em;"></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.34em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> Superior– intestine. Inferior– vagina
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><menclose notation="box"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="true"><mi mathvariant="normal">D</mi></mstyle></mstyle></mstyle></menclose></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\boxed{\mathrm{D}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.3633em; vertical-align: -0.34em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 1.0233em;"><span style="top: -3.3633em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3.3633em;"></span><span class="boxpad"><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">D</span></span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.0233em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3.3633em;"></span><span class="stretchy fbox" style="height: 1.3633em; border-style: solid; border-width: 0.04em;"></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.34em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> Lateral – broad ligaments, uterine tubes, and ovaries.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span> Uterus is supported to its position by: -
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><menclose notation="box"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="true"><mi mathvariant="normal">D</mi></mstyle></mstyle></mstyle></menclose></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\boxed{\mathrm{D}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.3633em; vertical-align: -0.34em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 1.0233em;"><span style="top: -3.3633em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3.3633em;"></span><span class="boxpad"><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">D</span></span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.0233em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3.3633em;"></span><span class="stretchy fbox" style="height: 1.3633em; border-style: solid; border-width: 0.04em;"></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.34em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> Pelvic floor and maintained in position by several ligaments.
&gt; Transverse /cardinal/mackenrodts ligaments, uterosacral ligaments, pubocervical ligaments- It attaches the cervix to the lateral pelvic wall by its attachment to the Obturator fascia of the Obturator internus muscle, and is continuous externally with the fibrous tissue that surrounds the pelvic blood vessels.
&gt; Broad ligaments- formed from folds of peritoneum which are draped over the uterine tubes. Hang down like a curtain and spread from sides of uterus to sidewalls of pelvis.
&gt; Round ligaments- maintains anteverted position of uterus. Arise from cornua of the uterus and in front of and below insertion of each uterine tube and pass between folds of broad ligament through inguinal canal to be inserted into each labium major.
&gt; Ovarian ligaments- begin at cornua of uterus behind uterine tubes and pass down between folds of broad ligament to ovaries. Round ligament, uterine tubes and ovarian ligament are very similar in appearance and arise from same area of uterus.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span> The following are the parts of the uterus: -
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><menclose notation="box"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="true"><mi mathvariant="normal">A</mi></mstyle></mstyle></mstyle></menclose></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\boxed{\mathrm{A}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.3633em; vertical-align: -0.34em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 1.0233em;"><span style="top: -3.3633em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3.3633em;"></span><span class="boxpad"><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">A</span></span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.0233em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3.3633em;"></span><span class="stretchy fbox" style="height: 1.3633em; border-style: solid; border-width: 0.04em;"></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.34em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> Body/corpus- makes upper 1/3 of the uterus and is the greater part.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><menclose notation="box"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="true"><mi mathvariant="normal">D</mi></mstyle></mstyle></mstyle></menclose></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\boxed{\mathrm{D}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.3633em; vertical-align: -0.34em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 1.0233em;"><span style="top: -3.3633em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3.3633em;"></span><span class="boxpad"><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">D</span></span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.0233em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3.3633em;"></span><span class="stretchy fbox" style="height: 1.3633em; border-style: solid; border-width: 0.04em;"></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.34em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> Fundus – doomed upper wall between insertion of uterus tubes. In midwifery fundus is essential in: -
&gt; Determining fundal height to assess fetal growth</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC
78</p>
<p>&gt; Assessing uterine contractions and progress of labor
&gt; Assessing uterine involution</p>
<p>☑ Cornua – upper outer angles of uterus where uterine tubes join the uterus
☑ Cavity – potential space between anterior and posterior walls. Changes in shapes, base of triangle being uppermost.
☑ Isthmus – narrow area between cavity and cervix 7mm long. Enlarges during pregnancy to form lower uterine segment jointly with the cervix.</p>
<p>Layers of the uterus includes: -
i. Endometrium
ii. Myometrium
iii. Perimetrium</p>
<p>i. Endometrium: -
Endometrium forms lining of ciliated epithelium (mucous membrane) on a base of connective tissue or stroma and its made up of simple columnar epithelium.
Endometrium is the innermost ciliated mucosal layer that contains numerous glands that secretes thin alkaline fluid that keep the uterine cavity moist.</p>
<p>In uterine cavity endometrium is constantly changing in thickness throughout menstrual cycle and it is made up two sub layers, namely</p>
<p>☑ Functional layer also known as stratum functionalis.
✓ It is the one that proliferate in readiness for implantation and it is the one that undergoes thickening.
✓ It is the layer that is shed during menstruation</p>
<p>☑ Basal layer also known as stratum basalis.
✓ It is the one that replaces functional layer each month
✓ It undergoes changes in response to hormones at different phases of menstrual cycle</p>
<p>ii. Myometrium: -
It is the middle muscular layer that is responsible for uterine contractions and thickest at the fundal region.
It is made up of three layers of smooth muscles.
Its muscle fibres runs in all direction and interweaves to surround blood vessels and lymphatic that passes to and from the endometrium. This is important because myometrial contraction after delivery helps in controlling bleeding.</p>
<p>Outer layer is formed of longitudinal fibers that are continuous with that of uterine tubes, uterine ligament and vagina.
In cervix muscle fibers are embedded in collagen fibers which enable it to stretch in labour.</p>
<p>iii. Perimetrium: -
It is the outermost double serous membrane attached to the broad ligament.
It is an extension of peritoneum draped over the uterus.</p>
<p>Blood supply, innervation and lymphatic drainage to the uterus
Arterial blood supply to the uterus is via: - Uterine artery which enters at the level of the cervix. It sends some branches to upper vagina then runs upwards in a twisted fashion to meet ovarian artery where it forms an anastomosis with it</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>near cornua. Ovarian artery is a branch of abdominal aorta and supplies ovary and uterine tube before joining the uterine artery.</p>
<ul>
<li>The venous drainage is through uterine veins. There are two uterine veins on each side of the uterus.</li>
<li>The Lymphatic drainage to the uterus is through Internal iliac glands drains uterine body and other pelvic lymph glands drain cervical area.</li>
<li>Innervations to the uterus is mainly through autonomic nervous system-sympathetic and parasympathetic via inferior hypogastric or pelvic plexus.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="functions-of-the-uterus">Functions of the uterus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-the-uterus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It acts as an organ of reproduction. Uterus functions as a site for reception, implantation, retention and nutrition of the fetus</li>
<li>It is an organ where menstruation occurs.</li>
<li>It is the site of uterine contraction for the expulsion of the fetus during delivery and to seal torn blood vessels after placental delivery.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="d-fallopian-tubes">d. Fallopian tubes: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#d-fallopian-tubes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>These are pair of tube like structures originating from the cornua of the uterus with distal ends located near the ovaries.</li>
<li>Also known as uterine tubes.</li>
<li>They are narrow tubes measuring approximately 4-inch (10 cms) extending from the ovary to uterus</li>
<li>Anatomical relation of the fallopian tubes includes: -</li>
<li>Anteriorly, posteriorly, and superiorly is the peritoneal cavity and intestines.</li>
<li>Laterally is the sidewalls of pelvis.</li>
<li>Inferiorly is broad ligament and ovaries.</li>
<li>Medially is the uterus.</li>
<li>Uterine tubes are held in position via the following: -</li>
<li>Attachment to the uterus</li>
<li>Infundibulopelvic ligaments.</li>
<li>Each tube has four parts: -</li>
<li>Interstitial portion(interstitium)-it lies within wall of uterus. It is approximately 1.25 cm with a lumen of about 1mm wide.</li>
<li>Isthmus – it is the narrowest part. It is about 2.5 cm long. It is the site for tubal ligation.</li>
<li>Ampulla-it is the widest portion of about 5cm long where fertilization takes place.</li>
<li>Infundibulum- it is funnel shaped end with many processes known as fimbriae that are in close proximity with the ovaries.</li>
<li>NB-Cornua is the region of the uterus where uterine tubes join the uterus. It is where uterine pace makers are situated.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="functions-of-the-fallopian-tubes">Functions of the fallopian tubes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-the-fallopian-tubes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Propels ovum towards uterus (The effects of cilia and peristalsis helps the ovum to move through the fallopian tubes)</li>
<li>Receives spermatozoa</li>
<li>Provides site for fertilization</li>
<li>Supplies the fertilized ovum with nutrition during its journey to uterus.</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-fe267f0a.jpeg" alt="img-19.jpeg">
A diagram showing female internal organs</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-9e0a6926.jpeg" alt="img-20.jpeg">
Figure 3 (b). Diagrammatic sectional view of the female reproductive system</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>e. Ovaries: -</p>
<ul>
<li>Ovaries are Almond shaped glandular organs located on each side of the uterus.</li>
<li>Ovaries are the site for oogenesis and endocrine function.</li>
<li>Ovary has the following layers: -</li>
<li>☑ Capsule of dense Connective tissue</li>
<li>☑ Cortex just deep to capsule contains follicles with egg cells (oocytes). It is surrounded by the stroma.</li>
<li>☑ Medulla is middle region composed of connective tissue, blood vessels and lymphatics.</li>
<li>☑ Tunica albuginea. Over this lies germinal epithelium modification of peritoneum. This forms germinal epithelium which is a peritoneal membrane covering the ovary</li>
<li>Anatomical relation to the uterus include: -</li>
<li>☑ Anterior-broad ligament</li>
<li>☑ Posterior-intestines</li>
<li>☑ Lateral-infundibulopelvic ligament and sidewalls of pelvis.</li>
<li>☑ Superior-uterine tubes</li>
<li>☑ Medial-uterus and ovarian ligaments'</li>
<li>Ovaries are supported by:</li>
<li>☑ Attached to broad ligament from above, supported by ovarian ligament medially and infundibulopelvic ligament laterally.</li>
<li>Blood supply, lymphatic drainage and innervation to the ovaries is through:</li>
<li>☑ Ovarian arteries and ovarian veins. Right ovarian vein drains into inferior venacava, but left ovarian vein drains into left renal vein.</li>
<li>☑ Lymphatic drainage is to lumbar glands.</li>
<li>☑ Nerve supply is from ovarian plexus.</li>
</ul>
<p>f. Ovarian follicles: -</p>
<ul>
<li>Ovarian follicles contain oocytes in various stages.</li>
<li>Ovarian follicles (specifically Granulosa cells) secrete estrogens that is responsible for: -</li>
<li>☑ Growth and repair of uterine lining</li>
<li>☑ Regulation of monthly female cycle</li>
<li>☑ Female sexual characteristics</li>
<li>☑ Maintenance of bone and muscle</li>
<li>☑ Other functions of oestrogen include:</li>
<li>It suppresses ovulation.</li>
<li>It inhibits lactation.</li>
<li>It assists water and electrolyte retention in the body.</li>
<li>Mature follicle is called graafian follicle.</li>
<li>Graafian follicle releases oocyte every month through ovulation.</li>
<li>After ovulation, empty follicle becomes a corpus luteum</li>
<li>Corpus Luteum secretes: -</li>
<li>☑ Progesterone – completes the preparation of uterine lining.</li>
<li>☑ Estrogens – Thickens the endometrium.</li>
<li>☑ Relaxin – relaxes uterine muscles and pubic symphysis</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>☑ Inhibin – decreases secretion of FSH and LH</p>
<ul>
<li>Corpus albicans is a white scar tissue left after the corpus luteum degenerate..</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="morphological-structure-of-graafian-follicle">Morphological structure of graafian follicle:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#morphological-structure-of-graafian-follicle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Graafian follicle is made up of the following features:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Theca interna</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Theca externa</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Granulosa cells</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Antrum</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Follicular fluid</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Theca interstitial cells.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Granulosa cells of the graafian follicle secretes estrogen which has several functions as discussed earlier.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Theca interstitial cells provides nourishment, structural support and development of vascular system necessary for follicle development.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Antrum contains follicular fluid</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-de35e421.jpeg" alt="img-21.jpeg">
A diagram showing graafian follicle.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="morphology-and-structure-of-human-ovum">Morphology and structure of human ovum: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#morphology-and-structure-of-human-ovum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The human ovum is composed of: -</li>
<li>☑ Corona radiata</li>
<li>☑ Present in freshly ovulated ovum and provides support and protection to the developing ovum. It also has a function of providing specific proteins in</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>☑ Zona pellucida—It is the outermost most layer of the ovum that controls sperm entry. It has other functions as discussed elsewhere in this handout.
☑ Plasma membrane (Viteline membrane)—Also help in creating further block to sperm entry into the ovum.
☑ Periveteline space—Creates an additional sperm entry control into the ovum.
☑ Ooplasm (Cytoplasm). Provides nutrients to the ovum
☑ Nucleus—Contains the genetic material.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-3c433345.jpeg" alt="img-22.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="female-reproductive-cycle">Female reproductive cycle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#female-reproductive-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Female reproductive cycles are controlled by hormonal changes occurring every by month.</li>
<li>These hormones are majorly from the hypothalamus, anterior pituitary and ovary</li>
<li>Reproductive changes occur in two major organs, the ovaries and the uterus. This provides two cycles.</li>
<li>☑ Ovarian cycle: Changes in ovary during and after maturation of the follicle and oocyte</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">□</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\square</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.675em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">□</span></span></span></span></span> Uterine cycle (menstrual cycle): These are changes that occurs within the uterus to receive fertilized ovum and implantation.</p>
<p>Hormonal control of the female reproductive cycle is through Gonadotropin Releasing Hormone (GnRH) which is secreted by the hypothalamus. It stimulates anterior pituitary to secrete Follicle Stimulating Hormone (FSH) and Luteinizing Hormone (LH). FSH and LH target the ovaries and drive the ovarian. Estrogens and progesterone from the ovaries drive the uterine cycle.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ovarian-cycle">Ovarian cycle.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ovarian-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are changes that occur with the ovaries in every reproductive cycle.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span> Ovarian cycle is made up of three phases, namely: -</p>
<p>i. Follicular phase
ii. Ovulation
iii. Luteal phase</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="i-follicular-phase">i. Follicular phase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#i-follicular-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">□</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\square</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.675em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">□</span></span></span></span></span> About 20 follicles are stimulated to develop at each reproductive cycle but only one reaches maturity
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">□</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\square</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.675em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">□</span></span></span></span></span> FSH from anterior pituitary is responsible for stimulating follicle growth.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">□</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\square</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.675em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">□</span></span></span></span></span> This phase leads to a mature (Graafian) follicle that will undergo ovulation.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">□</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\square</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.675em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">□</span></span></span></span></span> Granulosa cells of follicle secrete estrogens and inhibin
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">□</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\square</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.675em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">□</span></span></span></span></span> Increasing levels of estrogens and inhibin inhibit FSH
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">□</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\square</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.675em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">□</span></span></span></span></span> Increasing estrogens also stimulates secretion of LH
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">□</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\square</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.675em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">□</span></span></span></span></span> As ovarian follicle matures, it moves closer to the surface of the ovary.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ii-ovulation">ii. Ovulation: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ii-ovulation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">□</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\square</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.675em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">□</span></span></span></span></span> Ovulation is the rupturing of the graafian follicle to release the ovum
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">□</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\square</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.675em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">□</span></span></span></span></span> LH stimulates rupture of the Graafian follicle and release of oocyte from ovary into the pelvic cavity and fimbriae of fallopian tube picks up the ovulated oocyte into the uterine tubes.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">□</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\square</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.675em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">□</span></span></span></span></span> The follicle then ruptures expelling the ovum at mid cycle <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>14</mn><mtext>th</mtext></msup><mo>+</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">14^{\text{th}} + 1</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.9324em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">4</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8491em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">th</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">+</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">1</span></span></span></span></span> day of a 28 days' cycle.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">□</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\square</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.675em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">□</span></span></span></span></span> Anovulatory cycles sometimes occur. This means that there is no ovulation in this case but menstruation take place.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">□</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\square</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.675em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">□</span></span></span></span></span> Sometimes ovulation vary in timing ranging from <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>8</mn><mtext>th</mtext></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">8^{\text{th}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8491em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">8</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8491em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">th</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>20</mn><mtext>th</mtext></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">20^{\text{th}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8491em;"></span><span class="mord">2</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8491em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">th</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> day of menstrual cycle.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">□</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\square</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.675em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">□</span></span></span></span></span> Symptoms of ovulation</p>
<ul>
<li>Sharp cutting abdominal pain (mittleschmerz)</li>
<li>Raise in body temperature (0.2) for 1-2 days</li>
<li>Thick sticky elastic cervical/vaginal mucus</li>
<li>Endometrial proliferation.</li>
</ul>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">□</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\square</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.675em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">□</span></span></span></span></span> Mechanisms that leads to ovulation include: -</p>
<ul>
<li>LH Surge</li>
<li>Increase in intrafollicular pressure</li>
<li>Ischemia to the graafian follicle</li>
<li>Effects of proteolytic enzymes.</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="luteal-phase">Luteal phase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#luteal-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>It is also known as post ovulatory phase</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>LH stimulates development of Corpus luteum from ovulated or ruptured follicle however increasing levels of progesterone suppresses levels of LH.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Corpus luteum secretes mostly progesterone &amp; some estrogens</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Progesterone prepares endometrium for possible pregnancy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In case pregnancy does not occur: -</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ After about two weeks, corpus luteum atrophies to corpus albicans (white body)</p>
</li>
<li>
