<p>☑ Progesterone and estrogen levels decline and this decline makes the developing functional layer of the endometrium not to be supported hence menstruation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If pregnancy occurs, the developing embryo produces human chorionic gonadotrophin hormones. This hormone supports the development of corpus luteum. Corpus development is critical because it forms the main source of progesterone in the first 3-4 months before placenta is fully formed.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If pregnancy does not occur:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Increasing levels of progesterone cause negative feedback that inhibits LH secretion</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ After about two weeks' corpus luteum atrophies to corpus albicans (white body)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Progesterone and estrogen levels decline</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Functional layer of endometrium discharged into first five days of next cycle.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-5aa4bb8a.jpeg" alt="img-23.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-diagram-showing-ovarian-phases">A diagram showing ovarian phases<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-diagram-showing-ovarian-phases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="uterine-cycle">Uterine cycle.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uterine-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>These are changes that occur in the uterus in readiness for a possible implantation.</li>
<li>These are cyclic changes which occur in the endometrium of the uterus of a fertile female.</li>
<li>The changes aim at preparing the endometrium to receive a fertilized ovum</li>
<li>There are three phases in uterine cycle, namely: -</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><menclose notation="box"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="true"><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mstyle></mstyle></mstyle></menclose></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\boxed{\checkmark}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.3722em; vertical-align: -0.34em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 1.0322em;"><span style="top: -3.3722em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3.3722em;"></span><span class="boxpad"><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.0322em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3.3722em;"></span><span class="stretchy fbox" style="height: 1.3722em; border-style: solid; border-width: 0.04em;"></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.34em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>  Proliferative
Secretory
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><menclose notation="box"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="true"><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">×</mo></mstyle></mstyle></mstyle></menclose></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\boxed{\times}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.3467em; vertical-align: -0.4233em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.9233em;"><span style="top: -3.3467em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3.3467em;"></span><span class="boxpad"><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord">×</span></span></span></span></span><span style="top: -2.9233em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3.3467em;"></span><span class="stretchy fbox" style="height: 1.3467em; border-style: solid; border-width: 0.04em;"></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.4233em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>  Menstruation</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="proliferative-phase">Proliferative phase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#proliferative-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ Rising estrogen levels from the growing follicle stimulates growth of the functional layer of endometrium to 4-10 mm thickness
It follows menstruation and last until ovulation. <strong>Regenerative</strong> phase is the first few days when the endometrium is reforming.
☑ Under influence of oestrogen and consist regrowth and thickening of endometrium.
☑ At completion of the phase endometrium has two layers.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="basal-layers">Basal layers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#basal-layers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>above Myometrium. 1mm in thickness.</li>
<li>Never alters during menstrual cycle.</li>
<li>Consists of rudimentary structures for building up new endometrium.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="functional-layer">Functional layer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functional-layer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Contains tubular glands and is 2.5mm thick. Changes constantly according to hormonal influences of the ovary. There is development of <strong>Cuboidal ciliated cells</strong> covers the functional layer.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="secretory-phase">Secretory phase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#secretory-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ Corpus luteum of ovary secretes progesterone.
☑ Progesterone stimulates thickening of the functional layer of endometrium to 12-18 mm and become well vasculised ready for implantation thus increased blood supply into the endometrium.
☑ Functional layer becomes spongy in appearance coz glands are more tortuous.
☑ There is growth of endometrial glands and secretion of uterine milk.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="menstruation-phase-menses">Menstruation phase (menses)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#menstruation-phase-menses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ Decline in progesterone levels causes functional layer of endometrium to discharge resulting in vaginal bleeding called menstruation and last 3-5 days. This is because declining levels of progesterone interferes with the maintenance of functional layer, blood vessels to the functional layer diminishes in its function. This leads to ischemia to the functional layer thus necrosis.
☑ It's the terminal phase of the cycle when endometrium is shed to the basal layer along with blood from capillaries and unfertilized ovum.
☑ It marks the beginning of the next cycle.
☑ The menses are not coagulated (<strong>What is the reason for this?)</strong></p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hormones-that-controls-female-reproduction">Hormones that controls female reproduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hormones-that-controls-female-reproduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Main hormones that controls female reproduction include: -</p>
<p>Estrogen
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>▽</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\bigtriangledown</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord">▽</span></span></span></span></span>  Progesterone
Follicle stimulating hormone.
Luteinizing hormone
Relaxin
Prolactin
Oxytocin</p>
<p>NB-Read and write short notes on each of the above mentioned hormone (Review endocrine system lectures).</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="oogenesis">Oogenesis:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#oogenesis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is the process of ovum formation in the ovaries.
Germinal cells migrate to ovary and become potential egg cells called oogonia
In fetus, millions of oogonia produced by mitosis but most of them degenerate (atresia)
Some develop into immature egg cells called primary oocytes during fetal development
About 200,000 to 2 million present at birth, 40,000 remain at puberty but only 400 mature during a woman's reproductive life
Each month about 20 primary oocytes become secondary oocytes but usually only one survives to be ovulated from Graafian follicle.
Egg forming cells (oocytes) go through two divisions: -
☑ Primary
☑ Secondary</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span>  oogenesis starts with a diploid primary oocyte that divides, resulting in two haploid cells (one is a large secondary oocyte and one is a small  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>1</mn><mtext>st</mtext></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1^{\text{st}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7936em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">1</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.7936em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">st</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>  polar body that may itself divide).
Second division only occurs if secondary oocyte is fertilized. Results in one large haploid ovum (egg) and one smaller haploid  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>2</mn><mtext>nd</mtext></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">2^{\text{nd}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8491em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">2</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8491em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">nd</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>  polar body.
The ovum division starts and get arrested(stops) at prophase I until puberty.
After puberty, the ovum continues with cell division and again stops at... The ovum completes cell division only if fertilization occurs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-diagram-showing-oogenesis">A diagram showing oogenesis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-diagram-showing-oogenesis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-82e77413.jpeg" alt="img-26.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anatomy-and-physiology-of-female-breast-mammary-gland">Anatomy and physiology of female breast (Mammary Gland)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anatomy-and-physiology-of-female-breast-mammary-gland" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Breasts is a milk secreting gland composed of glandular tissue arranged in lobes (about 20 in number). Each lobe is divided into lobules that consist of alveoli and ducts.</li>
<li>It is situated on anterior chest wall on either side of the midline and lies between 2nd and 6th rib extending from sternum with tail at the axilla (axillary tail of Spence).</li>
<li>During pregnancy oestrogen are responsible for growth of duct system and progesterone for the increase of alveoli.</li>
<li>Prolactin is responsible for milk synthesis and production.</li>
<li>Under influence of oxytocin hormone, the myoepithelial cells contracts making the tubules shorter and wider.</li>
<li>The alveoli contain acini cells, which produce milk. The acini cells are surrounded by myoepithelial cells, which contract and relax to propel milk out.</li>
<li>Small lactiferous ducts, carrying milk from the alveoli, unite to form larger ducts. These are open by lactiferous ducts at the nipple. Several ducts (lactiferous tubules) conveying milk from one or more lobe emerge on the surface of nipple.</li>
<li>One large duct leaves the lobe and widens to form an ampulla (lactiferous sinus) which acts as a milk reservoir. These tubules are distensible and as they extend they provide a temporary reservoir for milk often described as lactiferous sinuses or ampullae.</li>
<li>Amount of adipose tissue determines size of breast</li>
<li>The nipple is composed of erectile tissue, which is covered with epithelium and muscle fibres. These muscles have a sphincter-like action which controls the flow of milk.</li>
<li>Around the nipple is an area of pigmented skin called the areola, which contains the Montgomery's glands. The glands produce sebum, which lubricates the breasts during pregnancy and throughout breastfeeding.</li>
<li>Suspensory (Cooper's) ligaments suspend breast from deep fascia of pectoral muscles.</li>
<li>Blood supply-internal and external mammary arteries branch from intercostal arteries. During lactation blood supply is increased. Drainage via corresponding veins which are arranged in a circular fashion around the nipple.</li>
<li>Lymphatic drainage through lymph nodes in axillae and mediastinum. The lymphatic drainage systems of the two breasts communicate freely. This accounts for the rapid spread of malignant growth from one breast to another.</li>
<li>The breasts have poor nerve supply and their function is controlled by hormones.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="physiology-of-lactation">Physiology of lactation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physiology-of-lactation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>During pregnancy, oestrogen and progesterone hormones stimulate the growth of duct and alveoli systems. Increased levels of oestrogen inhibit milk production.</li>
<li>Hormone production is reduced by delivery of the placenta at the end of the third stage of labour and this stimulates the anterior pituitary gland to release Prolactin, which initiates milk production.</li>
<li>The sucking reflex by the infant stimulates the production of oxytocin by the posterior pituitary gland.</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>The oxytocin causes the myoepithelial cells to contract and propel milk along the ducts.</p>
<p>Milk production and secretion is facilitated by:</p>
<ul>
<li>☑ Estrogens develop the ducts system in the breasts</li>
<li>☑ Progestrone develop the milk-secreting glands which are called alveoli</li>
<li>☑ Prolactin stimulate milk synthesis in the alveoli</li>
<li>☑ Oxytocin stimulate milk ejection from the alveoli</li>
</ul>
<p>Milk ejection (release from glands) is through: -</p>
<ul>
<li>☑ Nursing stimulates the hypothalamus to produce oxytocin</li>
<li>☑ Oxytocin secreted from the posterior pituitary</li>
<li>☑ Oxytocin causes smooth muscles around alveoli to contract and squeeze milk into lactiferous ducts, lactiferous sinuses and into the nipple</li>
<li>☑ Operated by positive feedback</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-05c23891.jpeg" alt="img-27.jpeg">
A diagram showing female breast</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="female-pelvis">Female pelvis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#female-pelvis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The bony pelvis is the largest bone in the body. Its basin shaped and situated in the lower portion of the trunk.</p>
<p>Functions of the pelvis include: -</p>
<p>Allows movement-walking and running
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  Permits one to sit and kneel, supports spinal column
Adapted for childbearing. Forms a bony passage through which fetus passes
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  Contains and protects reproductive organs.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  Articulates with the lumbar vertebrae above, with the heads of femur below, hence transmitting the weight of the body to the lower limbs and in a way maintaining body posture.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  Provides appropriate attachment sites for spinal, perineal and abdominal muscles. Also muscles of the lower limbs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pelvic-bones">Pelvic bones:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pelvic-bones" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Pelvic bones are: -</p>
<p>a) Two innominate bones(hipbones)
b) One sacrum
c) One coccyx</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-innominate-bones">A. Innominate bones: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-innominate-bones" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>There are two innominate bones namely: -</p>
<p>a) Ileum
b) Ischium
c) Pubis</p>
<p>The three innominate bones meet at the acetabulum.
Before an individual is 25 years of age, these bones have not ossified completely and appears as three distinct bones.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ileum">Ileum: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ileum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is the great flared out part.
The inside is smooth and the outside is rough and marks the attachment of muscles of the gluteal region.
It is curved on the upper border to form iliac crest.
Ileum has a concave anterior surface that creates the iliac fossa.
At the front of iliac crest there is a bony prominence known as anterior iliac spine.
Below it is anterior inferior iliac spine.
There are two similar points at the end of iliac crest namely posterior superior &amp; posterior inferior iliac spines.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ischium">Ischium: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ischium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is the thick(dense) lower part of Innominate bones.
It has two large inferior prominences.
Below iliac fossa there is iliopectineal line which ends in a rough swelling called iliopectineal eminence formed where the superior ramus of pubic bone meets Ilium.
It is the bone we sit on and forms the lowest part of the innominate bone.
It creates the posterior-inferior part of pelvis</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Ischium is the strongest part of the pelvis which holds the body weight in sitting up position
It has large inferior prominences called ischial tuberosities.
It has two ischial spines that are important in determining fetal station.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span>  Pubis: -</p>
<p>It is the smallest part of the pelvic bone with the superior and inferior rami.
The left and right join to form the pubic symphysis.
It forms the anterior part of the pelvis.
It has body and two oar-like projections referred to as superior and inferior ramus.
The two pubic bones meet at symphysis pubis to form the pubic joint and the pubic angle.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  Two inferior rami form the pubic arch merging onto a similar ramus on the ischium.
The space created by body of pubic bone rami and the ischium is called obturator foramen.
At the lower border of the Innominate bone, there are two curves.
One of the curve extends from posterior inferior iliac spine up to ischial spine and is called greater sciatic notch which is wide and rounded.
The other one lies between ischial spines and ischial tuberosity and is lesser sciatic notch.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="b-sacrum">B. Sacrum: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-sacrum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is a Wedge shaped consisting five fused vertebrae and forms the back of the pelvis.
The upper border of the  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>1</mn><mtext>st</mtext></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1^{\text{st}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7936em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">1</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.7936em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">st</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>  sacral vertebrae protrudes forward forming sacral promontory.
It has four sets of foramina that forms the exit of sacral nerves (cauda equina) to supply pelvic organs.
The anterior surface of sacrum is concave forming the hollow of sacrum.
On the other side of the sacral promontory are alae or wings of the sacrum.
Posterior surface is roughened to receive attachment of muscles.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="c-coccyx">C. Coccyx: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-coccyx" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is a small triangular shaped bone that give attachment to ligaments, muscle fibres of anal sphincter, ischiococcygeus muscle.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span>  Coccyx is a vestigial tail.
It consists of four vertebrae which may or may not be fused.
During labour it moves backwards to increase pelvic outlet.
It articulates with  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>5</mn><mtext>th</mtext></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">5^{\text{th}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8491em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">5</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8491em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">th</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>  sacral vertebrae to form sacrococcygeal joint.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pelvic-joints">Pelvic joints: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pelvic-joints" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>There are four pelvic joints, namely: -</p>
<p>a) One symphysis pubis
b) Two sacroiliac joints
c) One sacrococcygeal joint.</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>Pelvic joints are rigid in non-pregnant women, however during pregnancy and labour they become more mobile due to the influence of relaxin and progesterone hormones.</p>
<p>a) Symphysis pubis: -</p>
<ul>
<li>It is formed at the junction of the two pubic bones united by a plug of cartilage.</li>
<li>It widens during the last months of pregnancy diameter increasing from 4mm to 7mm and this may cause pain to a pregnant woman upon ambulation.</li>
</ul>
<p>b) Sacroiliac joint: -</p>
<ul>
<li>It is the strongest pelvic joint.</li>
<li>It is created through articulation of the sacrum and the ilium</li>
<li>During labour and pregnancy this joint relaxes increasing the diameter of the pelvic brim on the conjugate diameter.</li>
</ul>
<p>c) Sacrococcygeal joint: -</p>
<ul>
<li>Formed where base of the coccyx articulates with tip of sacrum.</li>
<li>Allows coccyx to more backwards during birth widening the outlet of the pelvis.</li>
</ul>
<p>Pelvic ligaments</p>
<ul>
<li>Each pelvic joint is supported together by ligaments-interpubic ligament at symphysis pubis, sacro iliac and sacrococcygeal ligaments.</li>
<li>Other important ligament in midwifery includes: sacrotuberous-from sacrum to ischial tuberosity, sacrospinous-from sacrum to ischial spine.</li>
<li>The two ligaments cross sciatic notch and forms posterior wall of pelvic outlet</li>
</ul>
<p>Pubic arch: -</p>
<ul>
<li>Pubic arch is formed through convergence of inferior rami of the ischium and pubis (Ischiopubic rami) on either sides.</li>
</ul>
<p>Pubic angle (Subpubic angle).</p>
<ul>
<li>It is formed by inferior borders of ischiopubic rami.</li>
<li>It is the distance between right and left ischial tuberosities.</li>
</ul>
<p>Iliopectineal line</p>
<ul>
<li>It is an iliopubic eminence created by the arcuate line from the ilium and pectineal line from the pubis.</li>
<li>It is the area that divides the pelvis into true and false pelvis.</li>
<li>It also forms the pelvic brim.</li>
</ul>
<p>Pelvic floor</p>
<ul>
<li>Formed by soft tissues that fill outlet of pelvis.</li>
<li>Most important is the strong diaphragm of muscle slung like a hammock from walls of pelvis where through it urethra, vagina and anal canal pass</li>
<li>Functions of pelvic floor includes: -</li>
<li>Supports weight of abdominal and pelvic organs.</li>
<li>Muscles are responsible for voluntary control of micturition and defecation and sexual intercourse.</li>
<li>During childbirth it influences passive movement of fetus through the birth canal and relaxes to allow exit of fetus from pelvis.</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>d) Creates a counter resistance during second stage of labour that help in delivery of the baby.
e) Muscles creates pump that promotes venous return from the pelvic region.
f) Helps in maintaining intra-abdominal pressure.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="muscle-layers-of-pelvic-floor">Muscle layers of pelvic floor<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#muscle-layers-of-pelvic-floor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Pelvic floor is made up of two layers of muscles, namely: -
a) Superficial layer
b) Deep layer</li>
</ul>
<p>a) Superficial layer is composed of:
a) External anal Sphincter - Encircles anus and is attached behind by few fibers to the coccyx
b) Transverse perineal muscles - From ischial tuberosities to centre of perineum
c) Bulbo-carvenosus Muscles - Pass from perineum forwards around vagina to corpora carvernosa of the clitoris just under pubic arch.
d) Ischio-carvenosus muscles pass from ischial tuberosities along pubic arch to corpora carvernosa.
e) Membranous sphincter of the Urethra - Composed of muscle fibers passing above and below urethra and attached to pubic bones. Not a true sphincter as it's not circular but acts to close urethra.</p>
<p>b) Deep muscle layers: -</p>
<ul>
<li>Deep layer is composed of three pairs of muscles which together are known as levator ani muscles because they lift or elevate the anus.</li>
<li>They are attached to either side of the pelvis (right and left).</li>
<li>These muscles include:
a) Pubococcygeus muscle - pass from pubis to coccyx with few fibers crossing over in the perineal body to form its deepest part
b) Iliococcygeus muscle - pass from fascia covering obturator internus muscle (white line of pelvis fascia) to coccyx
c) Ischiococcygeal muscles pass from ischial spine to coccyx in front of sacrospinous ligament.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pelvic-ligaments">Pelvic ligaments:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pelvic-ligaments" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Each pelvic joint is held together by ligaments. These ligaments are
a) interpubic ligament at symphysis pubis.
b) sacro iliac
c) sacrococcygeal ligaments.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Other important ligament in obstetrics includes:
a) sacrotuberous - from sacrum to ischial tuberosity
b) sacrospinous - from sacrum to ischial spine.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; NB: These two ligaments cross sciatic notch and forms posterior wall of pelvic outlet.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="anatomical-division-of-pelvis">Anatomical division of pelvis.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anatomical-division-of-pelvis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Pelvis is divided into two parts, namely:
a) False pelvis (Greater pelvis)
b) True pelvis (Lesser pelvis)</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="false-pelvis">False pelvis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#false-pelvis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ It is the portion above the pelvic brim.
☑ It does not take part in the mechanism of delivery and is of no obstetric importance.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="true-pelvis">True pelvis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#true-pelvis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ It is the portion that is below the pelvic brim.
☑ It determines the size and shape of the birth canal.
☑ It has brim, cavity and outlet.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pelvic-brim">Pelvic brim: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pelvic-brim" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It is Round in gynaecoid pelvis except where sacral promontory projects into it.</li>
<li>The posterior border of the pelvic brim is promontory and wings of sacrum.</li>
<li>The lateral border of the brim is iliac bones</li>
<li>The anterior border of the pelvic brim is pubic bones.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Major landmarks of the pelvic brim are:</strong> -</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Sacral ala or wing</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sacral iliac joint</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Iliopectineal line-edge formed at inward aspect of Ilium</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Iliopectineal eminence-roughened area formed where superior ramus of pubic bone meets Ilium</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Superior ramus of pubic bone</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Upper inner border of body of pubic bone</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Upper inner border of symphysis pubis</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Diameters of the pelvic brim are: -</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>a) Anteroposterior diameter (AP Diameter). This is from sacral promontory to upper inner border of symphysis.</p>
<p>☑ It has three dimensions, namely;</p>
<p>i. Anatomical conjugate diameter- From the uppermost point of symphysis pubis to sacral promontory. It is usually 12cm.
ii. Obstetrical conjugate diameter-From posterior border of upper surface to the sacral promontory. It is usually 11cm. It represents the available space for passage of the fetus.
iii. Diagonal conjugate-From lower border of symphysis to sacral promontory. It is 12-13cm (usually 1.25cm more than obstetric conjugate). It can be estimated on vaginal examination as part of pelvic assessment.</p>
<p>☑ NB: True conjugate is a term that is used to refer to both Anatomical conjugate diameter and Obstetrical conjugate diameter</p>
<p>b) Transverse Diameter:
✓ It is formed between points furthest apart on the iliopectineal lines and measures 13cm. Some structures pass through pelvic brim and may affect space available for fetus to pass e.g. descending colon</p>
<p>c) Oblique Diameter:
✓ It is the diameter formed from sacro-iliac joint to iliopectineal eminence. It usually measures 12 cm.</p>
<ul>
<li>NB: Sacrocotyloid dimension- passes from sacral promontory to iliopectineal eminence on each side and measures 9-9.5 cm. it is concerned with posterior position of occiput when parietal eminences of fetal head are stuck in the pelvis.</li>
</ul>
<p>Pelvic cavity: -
✓ It is formed by the pubic bones, ischium, ilium, and Sacrum.
✓ It extends from brim above to outlet below.
✓ Anterior wall is formed by pubic bones and symphysis pubis and it is 4cm in depth.
✓ Posterior wall is formed by curve of sacrum 12cm in length.
✓ Lateral walls formed by sides of pelvis mainly covered by obturator internus muscle.
✓ The cavity is circular in shape. Diameter is considered to be 12cm.
✓ The mid-cavity is at the level of the ischial spines.</p>
<p>Pelvic outlet
✓ It is diamond-shaped
✓ It is made up of the pubic bones, ischium, ischial tuberosities, sacrotuberous ligament, and 5th segment of sacrum.
✓ There are two outlets described as: -
a) Anatomical
b) obstetrical
✓ Anatomical Outlet- Formed by lower borders of each of the bones together with sacrotuberous ligament
✓ Obstetrical outlet- includes narrow pelvic strait through which fetus must pass. This strait lies between sacrococcygeal joint, 2 ischial spines and lower border of symphysis. Obstetrical outlet is the space between narrow pelvic strait and anatomical outlet. Pelvic outlet is diamond shaped.
✓ Diameters of the pelvic outlet include:
a) Anteroposterior diameter- from lower border of symphysis pubis to sacrococcygeal joint and measures 13 cm.
b) Oblique diameter- between obturator foramen and sacrospinous ligament. It measures 12cm.
c) Transverse diameter- between the 2 ischial spines, narrowest diameter in the pelvis. It measures between 10-11cm.</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>A Tables showing summary of pelvic diameters</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-diagram-showing-parts-of-the-pelvis">A diagram showing parts of the pelvis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-diagram-showing-parts-of-the-pelvis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-diagram-showing-parts-of-the-pelvis-and-pubic-arch">A diagram showing parts of the pelvis and pubic arch<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-diagram-showing-parts-of-the-pelvis-and-pubic-arch" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-classes-of-pelvis">Types (Classes) of pelvis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-classes-of-pelvis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span>  Pelvis is classified in two major ways, namely:</p>
<ol>
<li>Inherited- These are due to genetic predisposition and racial characteristics tics. The shape of brim defines the type of the pelvis under this classification.</li>
</ol>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  Major types under this category include: -</p>
<p>a) Gynaecoid pelvis
b) Android pelvis
c) Anthropoid pelvis
d) Platypelloid pelvis</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Acquired -These are as a result of diseases and conditions affecting pelvis especially during childhood.</li>
</ol>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  Major types under this category include: -</p>
<p>a) Rachitic pelvis.
b) Naegeles or asymmetrical pelvis
c) Roberts pelvis
d) Osteomalacic pelvis
e) Justo minor pelvis</p>
<p>a) Gynaecoid pelvis: -</p>
<p>It is the ideal pelvis favoring a normal delivery and child bearing.
It is found in about  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>50</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">50\%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">50%</span></span></span></span></span>  of all women.
It has the following features:</p>
<p>Rounded brim,</p>
<ul>
<li>Generous fore pelvis (part in front of transverse diameter).
Straight sidewalls</li>
<li>Shallow cavity with a broad, well curved sacrum.</li>
<li>Blunt ischial spines (Ischial spines not prominent).
Rounded sciatic notch.
Rounded Sub-pubic arch (Roman arch) and Sub-pubic angle of  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>90</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">90^{\circ}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6741em;"></span><span class="mord">9</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<ul>
<li>Sacrum curved</li>
<li>Obtuse greater sciatic notch</li>
<li>Triangular obturator foramen</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-android-pelvis">b) Android pelvis: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-android-pelvis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ It is the male-type pelvis.
☑ It is found in about 22.4% of women.
☑ It has the following features: -</p>
<ul>
<li>The Brim is heart-shaped with narrow fore pelvis.</li>
<li>Sacrum curved</li>
<li>Ischial spines prominent</li>
<li>Acute greater sciatic notch (sciatic notch narrow)</li>
<li>Oval obturator foramen</li>
<li>Sub-pubic arch very narrow [Gothic arch] less than 90°.</li>
<li>Transverse diameter is towards the back.</li>
<li>Sidewalls converge making it funnel shaped with deep cavity and straight sacrum.</li>
<li>Predisposes one to occipito-posterior position of the fetal head.</li>
</ul>
<p>☑ It is less suited for child bearing because of the following: -</p>
<ul>
<li>The heart shaped brim favors a posterior position of the occiput as a result of insufficient space for biparietal diameter in the narrow fore pelvis.</li>
<li>This is combined with the fact that the greater space lies in the hind pelvis.</li>
<li>Funnel shaped cavity may hinder progress in labour.</li>
<li>At outlet, prominent ischial spines sometimes prevent complete internal rotation of head and AP diameter becomes caught on them causing deep transverse arrest.</li>
<li>Narrowed subpubic angle can't easily accommodate biparietal diameter and this displaces head backwards</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c-anthropoid-pelvis">c) Anthropoid pelvis: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-anthropoid-pelvis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ It an Ape-like pelvis favoring OP positions often requiring operative vaginal deliveries.
☑ It is found in about 22.7% of women.
☑ It has the following features: -</p>
<ul>
<li>Has a long, narrow oval inlet.</li>
<li>Sacrum slightly curved.</li>
<li>Long-cone funnel pelvis with straight sidewalls.</li>
<li>Sidewalls diverge and sacrum is long and deeply concave.</li>
<li>Obtuse greater sciatic notch.</li>
<li>Oval obturator foramen.</li>
<li>Sub-pubic arch narrow.</li>
<li>Sciatic notch is very wide.</li>
<li>Has a long oval brim in which AP diameter is longer than transverse.</li>
<li>Ischial spines are not prominent.</li>
<li>Subpubic angle is also wide.</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>Labour doesn't present with difficulties but direct occipitoanterior or direct OPP is often seen in engagement and may persist to delivery.</p>
<p>d) Platypelloid pelvis: -
✓ It has the following features: -</p>
<ul>
<li>It has a kidney shaped brim.</li>
<li>Antero-Posterior diameter is reduced and transverse increased.</li>
<li>Sidewalls diverge.</li>
<li>Sacrum flat and cavity shallow.</li>
<li>Ischial spine blunt.</li>
<li>Sciatic notch and subpubic angle wide.</li>
<li>Often leads to cephalo-pelvic disproportion.</li>
<li>It is found in about 4.4% of women.</li>
<li>Triangular obturator foramen</li>
<li>Side walls are straight</li>
<li>Head must engage with sagittal suture in transverse diameter but usually descend through cavity without difficulty.</li>
<li>Engagement may necessitate lateral tilting of head (asynclitism) in order to allow biparietal diameter to pass the narrowest AP diameter of the brim.</li>
</ul>
<p>A Table showing differences in various types of pelvis.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Features</th><th>Gynaecoid</th><th>Android</th><th>Anthropoid</th><th>Platypelloid</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Brim</td><td>rounded</td><td>heart-shaped</td><td>long oval</td><td>kidney-shaped</td></tr><tr><td>Fore pelvis</td><td>generous</td><td>narrow</td><td>narrowed</td><td>wide</td></tr><tr><td>Side walls</td><td>straight</td><td>convergent</td><td>divergent</td><td>divergent</td></tr><tr><td>Ischial spines</td><td>blunt</td><td>prominent</td><td>blunt</td><td>blunt</td></tr><tr><td>Sciatic notch</td><td>rounded</td><td>narrow</td><td>wide</td><td>wide</td></tr><tr><td>Sub-pubic angle</td><td>90 degrees</td><td>&lt;90 degrees</td><td>&gt;90 degrees</td><td>&gt;90 degrees</td></tr><tr><td>Incidence</td><td>50%</td><td>20%</td><td>25%</td><td>5%</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
