<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="other-types-of-pelvis">Other types of pelvis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-types-of-pelvis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-rachitic-pelvis">a) Rachitic pelvis: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-rachitic-pelvis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  It is due to dietary deficiency of vitamin D causing rickets.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  Bones are excessively softened by the disease process, distorting the alignment due to weight of the body.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  Sacral promontory is forced inwards towards symphysis pubis while the lower end of sacrum swings backward and ischial tuberosities moves further apart.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> This increases all the diameter apart from AP diameter of the inlet.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Since brim is reduced and the preferred mode of delivery is C/S.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-naegeles-asymmetrical-pelvis">b) Naegeles/asymmetrical pelvis: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-naegeles-asymmetrical-pelvis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Results either from developmental anomalies or disease in childhood e.g. poliomyelitis.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Pelvis is characterized by unequal exertion of pressure on the growing pelvis.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Mostly associated with congenital hip dislocation or poliomyelitis or congenital trauma.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> There is inadequate development in the side of intense pressure leading to bony fusion.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> It is the type where one of the sacral wings is missing giving it an oblique shape.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c-robert-s-pelvis">c) Robert's pelvis: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-robert-s-pelvis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> It has no wings. This means that there is absence of alae or poor development of alae.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> It is generally contracted and C/S is always necessary for delivery.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> This leads to early fusion of sacroiliac joint hence brim is abnormally small.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="d-osteomalacic-pelvis">d) Osteomalacic pelvis: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#d-osteomalacic-pelvis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> It a rare deformity due to adult's rickets.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> It leads to gross contraction of the pelvis</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="e-justo-minor-pelvis">e) Justo minor pelvis: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#e-justo-minor-pelvis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> It is similar to Gynaecoid pelvis in miniature.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> It is found in woman of small stature.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> It is found in women of normal stature.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> All the diameters are reduced but are in proportion.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Outcome of labour depend on fetus.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Often these women have small babies and outcome is favorable.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> If fetus is large, degree of CPD will result.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> If malpresentation or malposition of fetus exists, CPD results.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="differences-between-female-and-male-pelvis">Differences between female and male pelvis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#differences-between-female-and-male-pelvis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a) The vertical height is less in female than in males
b) Sub-pubic angle is greater in the female than in males
c) Female sacrum is shorter, wider, less curved.
d) Female Ischial spines are less prominent and less curved.
e) Height of pubic symphysis is less in females
f) Greater sciatic notch and wider in females
g) Distance between symphysis pubis and anterior margin of acetabulum is greater in females than in males.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="perineum-perineal-boy">Perineum (Perineal boy)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#perineum-perineal-boy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Perineum is a pyramid of muscles and fibrous tissue situated between vagina and rectum.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> It is made up of fibers from muscles.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Apex (deepest part) formed from fibers of Pubococcygeus muscle which cross over at this point.</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>✓ Base is formed from transverse perineal muscles which meet in the perineum together with Bulbo-carvenosus in front and external anal sphincter behind.
✓ Perineal body measures 4 cm in each direction.
✓ It is the part that is supported during second stage of labour to avoid perineal tears.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fetal-skull">Fetal skull<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fetal-skull" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The foetal skull contains a delicate brain, which may be subjected to great pressures as the head passes through the birth canal</p>
<p>The landmarks of the skull are described as:</p>
<p>✓ The vault, which lies between the orbital ridges and the nape of the neck-bones are thin and pliable so as to allow for alterations of the skull at birth, composed of the occipital bone, two parietal bones and two frontal bones.
✓ The base -comprised of firmly united bones that protect the vital centres in the medulla.
✓ The face -composed of 14 small bones that are firmly united and cannot be compressed.
✓ The mentum, also called the chin.</p>
<p>The regions of the fetal skull include: -</p>
<p>✓ The occiput: It is the area which lies between the foramen magnum and the posterior fontanelle. The sub-occipital region is the part below the occipital protuberance. It is limited by the occipital bone.
✓ The vertex: It is the area bounded by the posterior fontanelle, the two parietal eminences and the anterior fontanelle. It is a quadrangular area bounded anteriorly by the bregma and coronal suture, posteriorly by the lambda and lambdoidal sutures and laterally by lines passing through the parietal eminences.
✓ The brow: It is an area bounded on one side by the anterior fontanelle and coronal sutures and on the other side by the root of the nose and supra-orbital ridges of either side.
✓ Face: It is the area bounded by the root of the nose and supra-orbital ridges and on the other, by the junction of the floor of the mouth with neck.
✓ Sinciput: it is the area lying in front of the anterior fontanelle.</p>
<p>The fetal skull is composed of the following: -</p>
<p>a) Fetal skull Bones which are: 2 parietal bones, 2 frontal bones, 2 temporal bones and one occipital bone.
b) Sutures which include: sagittal, frontal, lamboidal, coronal and temporal
c) Fontanelles which are: anterior (bregma) fontanelle and posterior (lambda) fontanelle.</p>
<p>Sutures: -</p>
<p>✓ Sutures are non-ossified membranes attached to the margins of flat bones of foetal vault where the skull bones are not joined together with each other.
✓ Sutures and fontanelles separate the bones of the skull from each other. This allows for a degree of moulding during labour and delivery.</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Sutures of the foetal skull include: -</p>
<p>a) Saggital suture-lies between two parietal bones. It joins anterior and posterior fontanelle. Saggital suture is important in determining position in cephalic presentation during vaginal examination.
b) Coronal suture: runs between parietal and frontal bones on either sides. Separates the frontal bones from the parietal bones.
c) Lambdoidal suture: Separates the occipital bone from the two parietal bones.
d) Frontal suture (Also known as metopic suture) - lies between two frontal bones. Becomes obliterated with time while the other sutures become fixed joints.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⋄</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\diamond</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">⋄</span></span></span></span></span> Fontanelles: -</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Fontanelles are wide gaps that are formed when two or more suture lines meet at one point.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Fontanelles includes:</p>
<p>a) Anterior fontanelle
b) Posterior fontanelle
c) Sphenoidal fontanelle
d) Mastoid fontanelle</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> NB: Only anterior and posterior fontanelles that have obstetrical importance.</p>
<p>a) Anterior fontanelle (Bregma): -</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Anterior fontanelle is formed by joining four sutures in mid plane. These include: -</p>
<ul>
<li>Anteriorly is frontal suture.</li>
<li>Posteriorly is the sagittal suture.</li>
<li>On either side are the coronal sutures.</li>
</ul>
<p>It is diamond in shape.
Its floor is made by a membrane.
It closes (Ossify) at 18mth after birth. (However may close as early as 9 to 12 months in some babies).
It measures about 3 to 4 centimeters long and 1.5 to 2 centimeters wide.
It is more pulsatile than posterior fontanelle.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Obstetrical significance of anterior fontanelle includes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Helps in determining the degree of fetal head flexion on vaginal examination
It facilitates the moulding of foetal head.
It helps in accommodating the marked brain growth.
It helps in determining intracranial status of the foetus/ newborn.</li>
</ul>
<p>b) Posterior fontanelle (Lambda): -</p>
<p>It is formed by junction of three sutures, namely: -</p>
<ul>
<li>Saggital suture anteriorly.</li>
<li>Lambdoidal suture on either side.</li>
</ul>
<p>It is triangular in shape.
Its floor is membranous but become bony at 3 months</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> It is less pulsatile than anterior fontanelle.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> It denotes the position of the head in relation to maternal pelvic.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diameters-of-fetal-skull">Diameters of fetal skull: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diameters-of-fetal-skull" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Suboccipital-Bregmatic Diameter = 9.5 cm: Which follows a line drawn from the middle of the anterior fontanelle to the under surface of the occipital bone just where it joins the neck. In full flexion the suboccipito-bregmatic diameter presents. (Vertex presentation)</li>
<li>Occipital-Frontal Diameter = 11.5 cm: A line extending from a point just above the root of the nose to the most prominent portion of occipital bone.</li>
<li>Submento-Bregmatic Diameter = 9.5 cm: From below the Chin to the centre of the Anterior Fontanelle. (Bregma). (Face presentation).</li>
<li>Mento-Vertical Diameter = 13.5 cm: From point of the Chin to the centre of the Posterior Fontanelle. (Brow presentation)</li>
<li>Suboccipito-frontal. From below the occipital protuberance to the centre or the frontal suture. = 10 cm</li>
<li>from below the occipital protuberance to the anterior end of the bregma.</li>
<li>Submento-vertical =11.5 cm</li>
<li>from the junction of the chin and neck to the vertical point which is a point on the sagittal suture midway between anterior and posterior fontanelles.</li>
<li>Biparietal Diameter = 9.5 cm: The greatest transverse diameter of the head, which extends from one parietal eminence to the other.</li>
<li>Bitemporal Diameter = 8.2 cm: The greatest distance between the two, (Left and Right) Temporal Sutures.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-diagram-showing-fetal-skull-diameters">A diagram showing fetal skull diameters<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-diagram-showing-fetal-skull-diameters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-65a7ae5a.jpeg" alt="img-40.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="key">KEY:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#key" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>SOB -Sub-occipitobregmatic. 9.5 cms
SOF -Sub-occipitofrontal. 10.0 cms
OF- Occipitofrontal. 11.5 cms
MV-Mentovertical. 13.5 cms

<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>Fetal skull moulding.</p>
<p>✓ Moulding is the process through which foetal skull bones come into contact with each other during delivery. This process is important in reducing fetal skull diameter to facilitate delivery. Though this process is important in assisting delivery, excessive moulding is an indicator of impeding danger associated with labour.</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="fertilization-implantation-embryology-and-foetal-development">Fertilization, implantation, embryology and foetal development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fertilization-implantation-embryology-and-foetal-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="learning-objectives">Learning objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#learning-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>By the end of the lesson the learner should be able to: -</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Explain the process of fertilization</li>
<li>Describe the process of implantation</li>
<li>Describe embryology and foetal development.</li>
<li>Discuss foetal circulation</li>
<li>Explain placenta at term and its variations.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fertilization-conception">Fertilization/ Conception<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fertilization-conception" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Other terms used to describe this phenomenon are fertilization, impregnation or fecundation.</li>
<li><strong>Definition</strong> - Fertilization is the union of the ovum and spermatozoa. Fertilization must occur fairly quickly after release of the ovum because it usually occurs in the outer third of a fallopian tube, the ampulla portion. Since the ovum is a non-motile cell, the following mechanisms assist it to move along the fallopian tubes:</li>
<li>☑ The action of cilia in the fallopian tubes</li>
<li>☑ The fallopian tubes peristalsis effect</li>
<li>The functional life span of a spermatozoon is about 48 hours; however, it may be as long as 72 hours or longer. Therefore, sexual coitus during this time may result in fertilization or pregnancy.</li>
<li>During sexual intercourse, approximately 300 million sperms are deposited into the female reproductive tract. Once the sperms are in the female reproductive, they undergo chemical, physiological and morphological changes that make the sperm more hyperactive. These physiological changes that the sperm undergoes to be able to fertilize an ovum is called capacitation.</li>
<li>Processes that leads to sperm capacitation include: -</li>
<li>☑ Change in the cell membrane lipid composition (lowering sperm cholesterol)</li>
<li>☑ Particular proteins and carbohydrates on the sperm are lost</li>
<li>☑ Certain proteins are phosphorylated (meaning they are active)</li>
<li>☑ Membrane potential of the sperm is lowered (from -30 Mv about -50 Mv)</li>
<li>The sperm that have undergone capacitation, swim faster towards the ovum.</li>
<li>Once the sperm reaches the ovum, it must penetrate through corona Radiata to reach the outer layer of the ovum, Zona pellucida.</li>
<li>After reaching the zona pellucid, the sperm undergoes acrosomal reaction. The acrosome releases its digestive enzymes. The cell membrane of the spermatozoa</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>fuses with the outer membrane of the acrosome creating pores that enables acrosome to release its content.</p>
<ul>
<li>The acrosomal enzymes start to dissolve zona pellucida creating pathway for the spermatozoa to get inside the ovum.</li>
<li>The major acrosomal enzymes that are released during acrosomal reactions are:</li>
<li>a) Hyaluronidase</li>
<li>b) Acrosin</li>
<li>c) Esterases</li>
<li>d) Neuraminidase</li>
<li>Following penetration by the sperm past the zona pellucida, the sperm bind itself to the plasma membrane of the ovum. The content of the sperm is completely taken into the cytoplasm of the oocyte.</li>
<li>Once the first sperm enters the cytoplasm of the oocyte, some changes occur in the membrane of the ovum that prevents further entry of sperms into the oocyte (to prevent polyspermy). These changes are called zona reaction.</li>
<li>Zona pellucida hardens once the first sperm penetrates to prevent further entry of sperms. At the same time, the ovum releases chemicals that that push other sperms away and creating an impenetrable fertilization membrane. The entry of sperm past zona pellucida causes the ovum to complete its second meiotic division and female pronuclei is formed. In summary, the following events occur once the sperm penetrates zona pellucida:</li>
<li>☑ Polyspermy block is created</li>
<li>☑ Hardening of zona pellucida takes place</li>
<li>☑ Completion of second meiotic division of the oocyte</li>
<li>☑ Un-packaging of male genetic material.</li>
<li>Once the spermatozoon is inside the oocyte, it un-packages its genetic material (23 chromosomes) and they spread into the Ooplasm of the oocyte.</li>
<li>The spermatozoon genetic material inside the oocyte re-organizes into male pronuclei (containing 23 chromosomes) with a membrane formed around it.</li>
<li>Spindle threads called microtubules forms between the male and female pronuclei and start to pull them towards each other. Finally, the two pronuclei fuse together completing the fertilization process forming a single diploid cell called a zygote.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="development-of-the-fertilized-ovum">Development of the Fertilized Ovum<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#development-of-the-fertilized-ovum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Immediately after fusion of male and female pronuclei, the resultant single diploid cell is now termed as a zygote. Zygote is the first diploid cell to form following fertilization.</li>
<li>Conceptus becomes the term used to refer to all materials derived from the fertilized zygote. It includes both embryonic and non-embryonic tissues. (i.e. placenta and fetal membranes).</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>The next stage after zygote formation is the cleavage of the zygote. Cleavage of the zygote results into two blastomeres. (Blastomeres are small cells that arise from early cell division). This cell early cell division is due to early mitosis which is promoted by mitosis Promoting Factor (MPF).</p>
<p>The next stage after cleavage is the Morula stage. At about third day, a cluster of about 16 cells is formed and this is what is now referred to as morula. After morula is formed, blastomeres become adherent to each other to form tight adherence and tight junction—this process is called compaction.</p>
<p>At around the 5th day, blastocyst in now formed. Blastocyst has got two identifiable cell types:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Outer cell layer/mass (trophoblast)—Around the outside of the blastocyst there is a single layer of cell known as the trophoblast that will form the placenta, placental membranes and the chorion. The Trophoblast later differentiate into two distinct layers namely: cytotrophoblast (inner layer) and syncytiotrophoblast (syncytium) and below this layer lies mesoderm or primitive mesenchyme. The syncitiotrophoblast is composed of nucleated protoplasm which is capable of breaking down tissue as in the process of embedding. The cytotrophoblast is a well-defined single layer of cells which initially produces a hormone known as human chorionic gonadotrophin (HCG), However later large amount of HCG is produced by syncytiotrophoblast.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Inner cell mass (embryoblast)—This is a mass of rounder cells that forms the entire embryo i.e. Fetus, umbilical cord and the amnion. Embryoblast further develops into hypoblast and Epiblast where a cavity called amniotic cavity emerges. This amniotic cavity lies on the side of the ectoderm. The yolk sac lies on the side of the endoderm and provides nourishment for the embryo until the trophoblast is sufficiently developed to take over. Embryoblast later forms the bilaminar embryonic disc.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>A fluid filled cavity called blastocoel is formed between embryoblast and trophoblast.</p>
<p>It should be noted that all these processes are occurring within the enclosure of the zona pellucida. The main reasons for maintaining zona pellucida up to the blastocyst stage are:</p>
<ul>
<li>To keep blastomeres together (Necessary for compaction)</li>
<li>To prevent premature implantation.</li>
</ul>
<p>The last stage of the fertilized ovum before implantation is the stage of blastocyst hatching. During this stage, the zona pellucida is lost. Trophoblast produces enzymes that digest zona pellucida and this is what leads to blastocyst hatching. The blastocyst hatching prepares blastocyst for implantation.</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>In general, the functions of zona pellucida are: -</p>
<ul>
<li>Species-species sperm penetration/recognition.</li>
<li>Permanent block to polyspermy</li>
<li>Act as porous selective filter</li>
<li>Act as an Immunological barrier</li>
<li>Keeps blastomeres together</li>
<li>Prevents premature implantation.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="implantation">Implantation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#implantation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Implantation takes place between 6-7th day after fertilization. The initial stage of implantation is adhesion of the blastocyst to the endometrial epithelium.</li>
<li>After fertilization:</li>
<li>Decidua develops</li>
<li>The implanted embryo continues to develop.</li>
<li>The fertilized ovum rolls and embeds itself onto the wall of the endometrium with embryoblast close to the endometrial layer. The trophoblastic tissues secrete hydrolytic enzymes that enables the blastocyst to bury itself deep into the functional layer of the endometrium.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-decidua">The Decidua<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-decidua" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>This is the name given to the endometrium during pregnancy.</li>
<li>After implantation, the rest of the endometrial layer becomes the decidua. There are three layers found in decidua, namely: -</li>
<li>Decidua basalis - This the part of the conceptus that forms at the base or point of implantation. It is the one that forms the maternal component of the placenta.</li>
<li>Decidua capsuralis - It is the part of the endometrial layer that grows to enclose the conceptus. It envelops the embryo during pregnancy. It diminishes as chorionic vesicles enlarge.</li>
<li>Decidua parietalis - It is the part of the endometrial tissues that fills the uterine cavity during pregnancy. It is the layer of the endometrial tissue that grows to fill the cavity of a pregnant uterus.</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-954062df.jpeg" alt="img-41.jpeg">
A diagram showing events occurring after fertilization</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-5c3b2cd9.jpeg" alt="img-42.jpeg">
A diagram showing implantation</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="embryo">Embryo<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#embryo" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Embryo is the term used to describe the period from fertilization to 8th week after fertilization.</li>
<li>Embryonic period is characterized by development of structures (organogenesis).</li>
<li>After fertilization Implantation the conceptus continues with erosion of maternal blood vessels creating pool of blood known as chorionic villi (Vacuoles). This creates the initial fetal-maternal blood exchange. Later this will form utero-placental circulatory system.</li>
<li>As the embryo is developing, at around 11th-13th day after implantation, cytotrophoblast cells penetrates syncytiotrophoblast forming primary trophoblast villi. The embryo Completes emersion into endometrium of uterus in the first 2 weeks after implantation.</li>
<li>Around the same time of 2nd week, the epiblast will form the Amniotic sac with the outer membrane forming the amnion and the inner membrane forming the amniotic sac cavity and the cavity will be filled with amniotic fluid.</li>
<li>At around 3rd week after implantation, there is gastrulation (Gastrulation is the process through which the developing embryo forms three germinal layers, namely:</li>
<li>a) The ectoderm is formed from migrating cells that replace the hypoblast and mainly forms the skin and nervous system</li>
<li>b) The mesoderm is formed between epiblast and endoderm and will later develop to form bones and muscles and also the heart and blood vessels, including those which are in placenta.</li>
<li>c) The endoderm is formed from epiblast cells that stay on dorsal surface and later develops into mucous membranes and glands.</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; NB:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The three germinal layers are developing from epiblast.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The events of forming germinal layers begins with formation of primitive steak on the surface of the epiblast.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>At around 16th week after implantation, extra embryonic mesoblast (Derived from epiblast and will later form placenta and other appendage organs) grows into primary trophoblast villi forming secondary villus.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>From 5-8 week, Embryo start to develop all structures of a human being and by the end of 8th week, the embryo has all structures that of an adult.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>From 9th week until birth, this period is referred to as foetal stage.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fetal stage is characterized by growth of formed structures.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In summary, the following events occur during embryo and fetal development: -</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>✓ 0 – 4 weeks: Primitive central nervous system forms. The heart develops and begins to beat and limb buds form.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> 4 - 8weeks: There is very rapid cell division. Head and facial features develop and all major body organs are in place in primitive form. Early movements are visible on ultrasound.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> 8 - 12 weeks: Eyelids fuse and kidneys begin to function. From 12 weeks the foetus begins to pass urine. Lanugo appears
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  Circulation functions properly and sucking and swallowing begin. External genitalia present
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  12 - 16 weeks: There is rapid skeletal development and meconium is present in the gut. Nasal septum and palate fuse.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  16 - 20 weeks: Mother feels foetal movements or quickening. Foetal heart is heard on auscultation.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  20 - 24weeks: Most organs are able to function and foetus responds to sound. The skin is red and wrinkled.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  24 - 28 weeks: May survive if born at this stage. There is respiratory movement and eyelids open.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  28 - 32 weeks: The testes descend into the scrotum. Foetus begins to store fat and iron. Skin becomes less wrinkled.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  32 - 36 weeks: The body is more rounded because of increased fat deposit and head hair is grown, nails reach finger tips and ear cartilage is soft.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  36 - 40 weeks: Skull is firm and contours rounded. Birth is due.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-diagram-illustrating-foetal-stage">A diagram illustrating foetal stage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-diagram-illustrating-foetal-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fetal-period">Fetal Period<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fetal-period" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Duration: Weeks 9 to 38 after conception (or until birth).</p>
<p>Major fetal events:</p>
<p>Organs grow in size and complexity.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-d7fcff34.jpeg" alt="img-43.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-8f1e21cb.jpeg" alt="img-44.jpeg"></p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-diagram-showing-derivatives-of-the-three-germinal-layers">A diagram showing derivatives of the three germinal layers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-diagram-showing-derivatives-of-the-three-germinal-layers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assignment">Assignment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assignment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

b) Neurulation (formation of neural plate, neural groove, neural tube, neural crest and cell induction).</p>

</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="development-of-placenta">Development of placenta<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#development-of-placenta" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Placental development begins at 6 weeks and is completed by  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>12</mn><mtext>th</mtext></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">12^{\text{th}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8491em;"></span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">2</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8491em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">th</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>  week.
Human placenta develops from two sources:</p>
<p>a) Fetal component- Chorionic frondosum
b) Maternal component- decidua basalis</p>
<p>As the pregnancy progresses the trophoblastic tissues and those from decidua basalis unites to form the placenta. Blood vessels develop forming hypogastric arteries that enters to the foetus through the umbilical cord as two arteries and there is one vein that also enters to the fetus through the same umbilical cord.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="umbilical-cord-also-known-as-funis">Umbilical cord (also known as funis)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#umbilical-cord-also-known-as-funis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Umbilical cord is a flexible tube like structure that connects the foetus to the placenta.</li>
<li>The umbilical cord begins to develop at around 5th week from the yolk sac and allantois.</li>
<li>It has an average length of about 50cm. A cord is considered to be short when it measures less than 40cm centimeters long and it is considered long if it measures more than 60 centimeters long</li>
<li>It has a diameter of 1-2 centimeters at term.</li>
<li>It has two arteries and one vein.</li>
<li>Vein carries oxygenated blood to the foetus</li>
<li>Arteries carry deoxygenated blood away from the foetus body.</li>
<li>The whole cord is covered in a layer of amnion continuous with that covering the placenta.</li>
<li>It has an outer smooth layer made up smooth muscles and an inner layer made up gelatinous substance(jelly) known as Wharton’s jelly that encloses the blood vessels.</li>
<li>The functions of Wharton’s jelly include: -</li>
<li>To protect umbilical blood vessels from injury</li>
<li>To insulate the umbilical blood vessels</li>
<li>It has immunological function</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="functions-of-placenta">Functions of Placenta<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-placenta" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a) <strong>Respiration</strong> - As pulmonary exchange of gases does not take place in the uterus the fetus must obtain oxygen and excrete carbon dioxide through the placenta</p>
<p>b) <strong>Nutrition</strong> - Food for the fetus derives from the mother’s diet and has already been broken down into forms by the time reaches the placenta site. The placenta is able to select those substances required by the fetus, even depleting the mother’s own supply in some instances.</p>
<p>c) <strong>Storage</strong> - The placenta metabolizes glucose and can also stores it in the form of glycogen and reconverts it to glucose as required. The placenta store iron and the fat soluble vitamins.</p>
<p>d) <strong>Excretion</strong> - The main substance excreted from the fetus is carbon dioxide; bilirubin will also be excreted as red blood cells are released relatively frequently.</p>
<p>e) <strong>Protection</strong> - It provides a limited barrier to infection with the exception of the treponema of syphilis and, few bacteria can penetrate. Viruses, however, can cross freely and may cause congenital abnormalities as in the case the rubella virus and HIV virus.</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>f) Endocrine function:</p>
<p>✓ Human chorionic gonadotrophin (HCG) is produced by the cytotrophoblastic layer of the chorionic villi.
✓ Oestrogen as the activity of the corpus luteum declines, the placenta takes over the production of oestrogen, which are secreted in large amounts throughout pregnancy.
✓ Human placental lactogeni (HpL) has a role in glucose metabolism in pregnancy.
✓ Progesterone</p>
<p>Appearance of the Placenta at Term</p>
<p>✓ The placenta measures about 20 cm in diameter
✓ It is about 2.5cm thick from its center.
✓ It weighs approximately one sixth of the baby's weight at term.
✓ It has two surfaces, namely: -</p>
<ul>
<li>The maternal surface maternal blood gives this surface a dark red colour and part of the basal decidua will have been separated with it. The surface is arranged in about 20 lobes which are separated by sulci.</li>
<li>The fetal surface. The amnion covering the fetal surface of the placenta gives it a whitish, shiny appearance. Branches of the umbilical veins and arteries are visible and spreading out from the insertion of the umbilical cord which is normally in the center.</li>
</ul>
<p>✓ The amniotic sac consists of a double membrane., namely: -</p>
<p>a) Chorion
b) Amnion</p>
<p>a) Chorion</p>
<p>☑ It is the layer adherent to the uterine wall.
☑ It peels up to the edge of the placenta.
☑ It is fragile and easy to tear
☑ It is opaque</p>
<p>b) Amnion.</p>
<p>☑ It is the membrane on the fetal side.
☑ It gives the placenta its typical shiny appearance.
☑ Protects the fetus from any infection.
☑ It peels up to the insertion of the cord
☑ It is thin but tough and hard to tear.
☑ It is translucent
☑ It contains the amniotic fluid.
☑ Amniotic fluid:</p>
<ul>
<li>It is a clear and pale straw in colour.</li>
</ul>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<ul>
<li>It constitutes 99% water and the remaining 1% is dissolved organic matters including substances and waste products.</li>
<li>It secreted by the amnion and fetal urine also contributes to the volume from the 10th weeks of the gestation onwards.</li>
<li>The total amount of amniotic fluid is about 1 litter and diminished to 800ml at 38 weeks of gestation (term). I</li>
<li>If the total amount exceeds 1500 ml, the condition is known as polyhydramnios</li>
<li>If less than 500mls it is known as oligohydramnios.</li>
</ul>
<p>✓ Function of the amniotic fluid:
a) Provides nutrients to the developing foetus.
b) Allows for free movement of the fetus
c) Protects the fetus from injury (Act as shock absorber)
d) Maintains a constant temperature for the fetus
e) During labour it protects the placenta and umbilical cord from the pressure of uterine contraction
f) Aids effacement of the cervix and dilation of the cervical Os.
g) Promotes fetal lungs development
h) Promotes development of foetal gastro-intestinal system.
i) Promotes bone and muscle development.
j) Provides lubrication of foetal parts. This prevents body part adhesions and webbing.
k) It has immunological function (Prevents infection to the foetus)</p>
<p>Anatomical Variations of the Placenta and the Cord
a) Succenturiate lobe of placenta (extra lobe/ accessory lobe)
✓ A small extra lobe is present, separate from the main placenta and joined to it by blood vessels which run through the membrane to reach it.
✓ The danger is that this small lobe may be retained in utero after delivery, and if it is not removed it may lead to hemorrhage and infection.
✓ Identification: It is noted on inspection, the placenta will appear torn at the edge, or torn blood vessels may extend beyond the edge of the placenta.</p>
<p>b) Circumvallate placenta
✓ In this situation an opaque ring is seen on the fetal surface. It is formed by a doubling back of the chorion and amnion.
✓ Danger may result in the membranes leaving the placenta nearer the center instead of at the edge as usually.</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>c) Battledore insertion of the cord. (Marginal insertion of the cord).</p>
<p>☑ The cord in this case is attached at the very edge of the placenta in the manner of the table tennis bat.
☑ Danger Likely it is detached up on applying traction during active management of the third stage of labour.</p>
<p>d) Lateral cord insertion</p>
<p>☑ This when the cord is inserted at some distance from the edge of the placenta. Perhaps midway between the central point of the placenta and the edge of the placenta.
☑ Danger: it leads to fetal blood flow decrease.</p>
<p>e) Central insertion of the cord:</p>
<p>☑ In this the cord is inserted at the middle of the placenta.</p>
<p>f) Velamentous insertion of the cord</p>
<p>☑ It is inserted into the membranes some distance from the edge of the placenta. The umbilical vessels run through the membranous from the cord to the placenta.
☑ Danger The vessels may tear with cervical dilatation and would result in sudden blood loss.</p>
<p>g) Bipartite Placenta</p>
<p>☑ Two complete and separate lobes are present, each with a cord leaving it.
☑ The bipartite cord joins a short distance from the two parts of the placenta.
☑ Danger-The extra lobe may be retained during delivery.</p>
<p>h) Tripartite placenta</p>
<p>☑ Three complete and separate lobes are present, each with a cord leaving it. The tripartite cord joins a short distance from the three parts of the placenta.
☑ Danger-The extra lobe may be retained during delivery.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-ef32aa6f.jpeg" alt="img-46.jpeg"></p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>Succenturiate lobe of placenta insertion of the cord</p>
<p>Battledore</p>
