<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="g-placenta-infarction">g) Placenta infarction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#g-placenta-infarction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ Placental infarction occurs when the blood supply to an area of the placenta is blocked and tissue necrosis results. It appears most commonly on the maternal surfaces.
It is mainly associated with vascular disease of the utero- placental unit secondary to maternal hypertension.
☑ As the infarct at area becomes necrotic, fetal circulation is reduced because blood flow through the placenta will decrease. However, if the circulation</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>through the rest of the organ is sufficient, a fetus may survive when as much as 20% to 30% of the placenta is infracted.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="h-placental-tumors-hemangiomata-of-the-placenta">h) Placental tumors (Hemangiomata of the Placenta)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#h-placental-tumors-hemangiomata-of-the-placenta" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ These tumors are relatively common, being found in approximately 1 percent of all placentas.</p>
<p>☑ Most tumors are small and without clinical significance but a few are large and associated with polyhydramnios, antepartum hemorrhage and premature labour.</p>
<p>☑ Most of these tumors are benign.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="i-placental-calcification">i) Placental calcification<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#i-placental-calcification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ Placental calcifications occur due to deposition of calcium on the maternal placental surface.</p>
<p>☑ This deposition of calcium on the maternal surface of placenta makes the placenta to have white patches due to formation of fibrous tissue.</p>
<p>☑ Major causes of placental calcifications include: -</p>
<ul>
<li>Post-datism</li>
<li>Maternal disorders eg DM, Vascular diseases etc</li>
<li>Cigarette smoking during pregnancy</li>
<li>Rh sensitization</li>
<li>Placental infections</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="j-other-pathologies-of-the-placenta-include">j) Other pathologies of the placenta include:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#j-other-pathologies-of-the-placenta-include" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ Syphilitic placenta- Due to congenital syphilis</p>
<p>☑ Edematous Placenta-It is the accumulation of fluid within the placental tissue.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-fetal-circulation">The Fetal Circulation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-fetal-circulation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>✓ During intrauterine foetal life, foetal lungs are not mature and are therefore not able to oxygenate blood. This fact therefore, calls for modification of intrauterine fetal circulation.</p>
<p>✓ To enable this, happen, there are temporary structure present in foetal circulation. They include: -
a) Placenta
b) Hypogastric arteries
c) Umbilical cord and its blood vessels (Two arteries and one vein).
d) Ductus venosus
e) Ductus arteriosus
f) Foramen ovale.</p>
<p>✓ The Umbilical Vein: Leads from the umbilical cord to the underside of the liver and carries blood rich in oxygen and nutrients. It has a branch which joins the portal vein and supplies the liver.</p>
<p>✓ The ductus venosus (from a vein to a vein). This is a structure within the fetal liver and it connects the umbilical vein to the inferior venacava from the portal</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<p>vein. At this point the blood mixes with deoxygenated blood returning from the lower parts of the body. Thus the blood throughout the body is at best partially oxygenated.</p>
<p>✓ The foramen ovale (oval opening): It is a temporary opening between the atrium which allows the majority of blood entering the foetal heart from the inferior venacava to pass across into the left atrium.
✓ The reason for this diversion is that the blood does not need to pass through the lungs since it is already oxygenated.
✓ The ductus arteriosus (from an artery to an artery): leads from the bifurcation of the pulmonary artery to the descending aorta, entering it just beyond the point where the subclavian and carotid arteries leave. It connects the pulmonary artery with the aorta.
✓ The hypogastric arteries: These arteries branch off from the internal iliac arteries and become umbilical arteries when they enter the umbilical cord. They return blood to the placenta. This is the only vessel in the fetus which carries unmixed blood.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-diagram-showing-foetal-circulation">A diagram showing foetal circulation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-diagram-showing-foetal-circulation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251225-7e1c994b.jpeg" alt="img-50.jpeg">
Fetal Circulation</p>
<p>Reproductive health Lecture notes. Rugendo.M.M @2018 Kabarnet KMTC</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="description-of-foetal-circulation">Description of foetal circulation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#description-of-foetal-circulation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>☑ Placenta forms the utero-placental unit through which foetal circulation is centered and because foetal lungs are not functional, placenta forms a unit in which maternal side help to oxygenate foetal blood.</p>
<p>☑ Oxygenated blood from the placenta passes through umbilical vein through the liver. In the liver, it connects with ductus venosus. Ductus venosus connects the blood into the inferior venacava. The blood mixes with deoxygenated from other parts of the body.</p>
<p>☑ Then blood gets into the right atrium. Once the blood is in the right atrium, majority of this blood flows directly into the right atrium via foramen ovale.</p>
<p>☑ Once in the right atrium, then blood is pumped to the entire foetal body.</p>
<p>☑ Some small amount is pumped through pulmonary artery; however, this blood does not reach foetal lungs but it is shunted to the aorta through ductus arteriosus.</p>
<p>☑ Finally, the blood from the foetal body system, will flow back to the placenta for further oxygenation through the umbilical arteries.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="adaptation-to-extra-uterine-life">Adaptation to extra Uterine life<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adaptation-to-extra-uterine-life" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>☑ At birth the baby takes a breath and blood is drawn to the lungs through the pulmonary arteries. It is then collected and returned to the left atrium via the pulmonary veins resulting in a sudden inflow of blood.</p>
<p>☑ The placental circulation ceases soon after birth and so less blood returns to the right side of the heart. In this way the pressure in the left side of the heart is greater while that in the right side of the heart becomes less. This results in the closure of a flop over the foramen ovale which separated the two sides of the heart and stops the blood flowing from right to left.</p>
<p>☑ Delivery of the placenta during child birth causes cessation of the placenta circulation resulting into the collapse of the umbilical vein, the ductus venosus and the hypogastric arteries.</p>
<p>☑ These vessels after collapsing, changes and becomes the following structures.</p>
<p>a) The umbilical vein becomes the ligamentum teres
b) The ductus venosus becomes the ligamentum venosum
c) The ductus arteriosus becomes the ligamentum arteriosum
d) The foramen ovale becomes the Fossa ovalis
e) The hypogastric arteries become the obliterated hypogastric arteries</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assignment">Assignment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assignment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
